\begin{split} \mathsf{VER}_{\mathrm{init}} \big( ek', vk, vk', coin_{\mathrm{init}} \big) \colon & \mathrm{Return} \ 1 \ \mathrm{iff} \ \mathrm{the} \ \mathrm{following} \ \mathrm{hold} \colon \ /\!/ \ coin_{\mathrm{init}} \ \mathit{as} \ \mathit{in} \ (1) \\ & - \ \mathsf{C.Verify} \big( ck, \mathsf{S'.Verify}(vk', \cdot, \cdot) = 1, c_{pk}^0, c_{\mathrm{cert}}^0, \pi_{\mathrm{cert}}^0 \big) \\ & - \ \mathsf{C.Verify} \big( ck, \mathsf{S.Verify}(vk, \cdot, \cdot) = 1, c_M, c_{\sigma}^0, \pi_{\sigma}^0 \big) \\ & - \ \mathsf{C.Verify}_{\mathrm{sn,init}} \big( ck, c_{pk}^0, c_{\mathrm{sn}}^0, c_M, \pi_{\mathrm{sn}}^0 \big) \ \land \ \mathsf{C.E'.Verify}_{\mathrm{enc}} \big( ck, ek', c_{\mathrm{sn}}^0, \tilde{c}_{\mathrm{sn}}^0, \tilde{\pi}_{\mathrm{sn}}^0 \big) \end{split}
```

Standard components of a coin are of the form

<span id="page-22-1"></span>
$$coin_{std} = (c_{pk}^i, c_{cert}^i, \pi_{cert}^i, c_{sn}^i, \pi_{sn}^i, c_{tag}^i, \pi_{tag}^i, \varepsilon, \varepsilon, \varepsilon, \tilde{c}_{sn}^i, \tilde{\pi}_{sn}^i, \tilde{c}_{tag}^i, \tilde{\pi}_{tag}^i),$$
 (2)

and instead of M and the bank's signature they contain a commitment  $c_{tag}$  and an encryption  $\tilde{c}_{tag}$  of the tag produced by the spender (and a proof  $\pi_{tag}$  of validity and  $\tilde{\pi}_{tag}$  proving that the values in  $c_{tag}$  and  $\tilde{c}_{tag}$  are equal). A coin is verified by checking the validity and consistency of each two consecutive components. If the first is an initial component then the values  $c_{tag}^{i-1}$ ,  $m_{tag}^{i-1}$ ,  $m_{tag}^{i-1}$  and  $m_{tag}^{i-1}$  are  $\epsilon$ ; if it is a standard component then  $c_M$ ,  $c_{\sigma}^{i-1}$  and  $m_{\sigma}^{i-1}$  are  $\epsilon$ .

{23}------------------------------------------------

$$\begin{aligned} \mathsf{VER}_{\mathrm{std}} \big( ek, \mathsf{v}k', \big( c_{pk}^{i-1}, c_{cert}^{i-1}, \pi_{cert}^{i-1}, c_{\mathrm{sn}}^{i-1}, \pi_{\mathrm{sn}}^{i-1}, \underline{c_{tag}^{i-1}}, \underline{\pi_{tag}^{i-1}}, c_{M}, c_{\sigma}^{i-1}, \pi_{\sigma}^{i-1}, \tilde{c}_{\mathrm{sn}}^{i-1}, \\ \tilde{\pi}_{\mathrm{sn}}^{i-1}, \tilde{c}_{tag}^{i-1}, \tilde{\pi}_{tag}^{i-1} \big), coin_{\mathrm{std}} \big) \colon \ /\!/ \ coin_{\mathrm{std}} \ \ as \ in \ (2) \end{aligned}$$

Return 1 iff the following hold:

- $-\ heonein$ C.Verify $(ck,\mathsf{S}'.\mathsf{Verify}(vk',\cdot,\cdot)=1,c^i_{pk},c^i_{cert},\pi^i_{cert})$
- $\mathsf{C.Verify}_{\mathrm{sn}}\big(ck, c^i_{pk}, c^i_{\mathrm{sn}}, \pi^i_{\mathrm{sn}}\big) \ \land \mathsf{C.Verify}_{\mathrm{tag}}\big(ck, c^{i-1}_{pk}, c^{i-1}_{\mathrm{sn}}, c^i_{\mathrm{sn}}, c^i_{\mathrm{tag}}, \pi^i_{\mathrm{tag}}\big)$
- C.E.Verify $_{\mathrm{enc}} \left( ck, ek, c_{\mathrm{sn}}^i, \tilde{c}_{\mathrm{sn}}^i, \tilde{\pi}_{\mathrm{sn}}^i \right) \ \wedge \ \mathsf{C.E.Verify}_{\mathrm{enc}} \left( ck, ek, c_{tag}^i, \tilde{c}_{tag}^i, \tilde{\pi}_{tag}^i \right)$

Our scheme. We now formally define our transferable e-cash scheme.

```
ParamGen(1^{\lambda}):
```

- $-Gr \leftarrow \mathsf{GrGen}(1^{\lambda})$

Recall that par is an implicit input to all other algorithms; we assume that they parse par as  $(1^{\lambda}, Gr, par_{S}, par_{S'}, par_{T}, ck)$ .

 $\mathsf{VfyGuilt}(pk_\mathsf{T}, \Pi)$ : Return  $\mathsf{T.VfyGuilt}(pk_\mathsf{T}, \Pi)$ 

### 5.3 Correctness and security analysis

Theorem 7. Our transferable e-cash scheme satisfies all correctness properties and is perfectly sound.

The first four correctness properties follow in a straightforward way from the correctness properties of S, S' and C, and verifiability of T. The fifth property follows from the fact that  $sk_{\mathcal{D}}$  has the form of a user secret key.

Because a user verifies the validity of all components of a coin before accepting it, perfect soundness of our scheme is a direct consequence of the correctness properties of S, S' and C, as well as perfect soundness of C and verifiability of T.

Detailed proofs of the following theorems can be found in Appendix A. We omit the proof for u-an as it is analogous to the one for c-an.

**Theorem 8.** Let  $\mathcal{N}$  be the nonce space and  $\mathcal{S}$  be the space of signatures of scheme S. Let  $\mathcal{A}$  be an adversary that wins the **unforgeability** game with advantage  $\epsilon$  and makes at most d calls to BDepo. Suppose that C is perfectly sound and  $(\mathcal{M} \cup \mathcal{S})$ -extractable. Then there exist adversaries against the unforgeability of the signature schemes S and S' with advantages  $\epsilon_{sig}$  and  $\epsilon'_{sig}$ , resp., such that

$$\epsilon \le \epsilon_{\rm sig} + \epsilon'_{\rm sig} + d^2/|\mathcal{N}|.$$

Assume that during the adversary's deposits the bank never picks the same final nonce twice. (The probability that there is a collision is at most  $d^2/|\mathcal{N}|$ .) In this case, there are two ways for the adversary to win:

(1) CheckDS outputs  $\bot$ , or an invalid proof, or an unregistered user: Suppose that, during a BDepo call for a coin c, CheckDS does not return a coin list. Recall that, by assumption, the final part (chosen by the bank at deposit) of the serial number of c is fresh. Since CheckDS runs T.Detect, by soundness of C and two-extractability of T, this will output a pair  $(pk, \Pi)$ , such that VfyGuilt $(pk, \Pi) = 1$ . Since a coin contains a commitment to a certificate for the used tag key (and proofs of validity), we can, again by soundness of C, extract an S'-signature on

{26}------------------------------------------------

pk. Now if pk is not in UL, then it was never signed by the bank, and A has thus broken unforgeability of S 0 .

(2) q<sup>W</sup> < |DCL|: If the adversary creates a valid coin that has not been withdrawn, then by soundness of C, we can extract a signature by the bank on a new initial serial number and therefore break unforgeability of S.

Theorem 9. Let A be an adversary that wins the game exculpability with advantage and makes u calls to the oracle URegist. Then there exist adversaries against mode-indistinguishability of C and tag-exculpability of T with advantages m-ind and t-exc, resp., such that

$$\epsilon \leq \epsilon_{\text{m-ind}} + u \cdot \epsilon_{\text{t-exc}}.$$

An incrimination proof in our e-cash scheme is simply an incrimination proof of the tag scheme T. Thus, if the reduction correctly guesses the user u that will be wrongfully incriminated by A (which it can with probability 1/u), then we can construct an adversary against exculpability of T. The term m-ind comes from the fact that we first need to switch C to hiding mode, so we can simulate πsn and πtag for the target user, since the oracles O<sup>1</sup> and O<sup>2</sup> in the game for tag exculpability (see Fig. [7\)](#page-19-0) do not return sn-pf and t-pf.

Theorem 10. Let A be an adversary that wins the coin anonymity game (c-an) with advantage and let k be an upper-bound on the number of users transferring the challenge coins. Then there exist adversaries against modeindistinguishability of C and tag-anonymity of T with advantages m-ind and t-an, resp., such that

$$\epsilon \leq 2 (\epsilon_{\text{m-ind}} + (k+1) \epsilon_{\text{t-an}}).$$

Theorem 11. Let A be an adversary that wins the user anonymity game (u-an) with advantage and let k be a bound on the number of users transferring the challenge coin. Then there exist adversaries against mode-indistinguishability of C and tag-anonymity of T with advantages m-ind and t-an, resp., such that

$$\epsilon \leq 2 \epsilon_{\text{m-ind}} + (k+1) \epsilon_{\text{t-an}}.$$

In the proof of both theorems, we first define a hybrid game in which the commitment key is switched to hiding mode (hence the loss m-ind, which occurs twice for b = 0 and b = 1). All commitments are then perfectly hiding (and proofs reveal nothing either) and the only information contained in a coin are the serial numbers and tags. They are encrypted, but the adversary, impersonating the bank, can decrypt them.

We then argue that, by tag anonymity of T, the adversary cannot link a user to a pair (sn,tag), even when it knows the users' secret keys. We define a sequence of k + 1 hybrid games (as k transfers involve k + 1 users); going through the user vector output by the adversary, we can switch, one by one, all users from the first two the second vector. Each switch can be detected by the adversary with probability at most t-an. Note that the additional factor 2 for t-an in game c-an is due to the fact that there are two coins for which we switch users, whereas there is only one in game u-an.

{27}------------------------------------------------

Theorem 12. Let A be an adversary that wins the coin-transparency game (c-tr) with advantage , let ` be the size of the two challenge coins, and k be an upper-bound on the number of users transferring the challenge coins. Then there exist adversaries against mode-indistinguishability of C, tag-anonymity of T, IACR-security of E and RCCA-security of E <sup>0</sup> with advantages m-ind, t-an, iacr and rcca, resp., such that

$$\epsilon \leq 2 \epsilon_{\text{m-ind}} + (k+1) \epsilon_{\text{t-an}} + (2 \ell + 1) \epsilon_{\text{iacr}} + \epsilon_{\text{rcca}}.$$

The crucial difference to the previous anonymity theorems is that the bank is honest (which makes this strong notion possible). We therefore must rely on the security of the encryptions, for which the reduction thus does not know the decryption key. At the same time, the reduction must be able to detect doublespendings, when the adversary deposits coins. Since we use RCCA encryption, the reduction can do so by using its own decryption oracle.

As for c-an and u-an, the reduction first makes all commitments perfectly hiding and proofs perfectly simulatable (which loses m-ind twice). Since all ciphertexts in the challenge coin given to the adversary are randomized, the reduction can replace all of them, except the initial one, by IACR-security of E. (Note that in the game these ciphertexts never need to be decrypted.) The factor 2` is due to the fact that there are at most ` encryptions of SN/tag pairs. Finally, replacing the initial ciphertext (the one that enables detection of doublespending) can be done by a reduction to RCCA-security of E 0 : the oracle Depo<sup>0</sup> can be simulated by using the reduction's own oracles Dec and GDec (depending on whether Depo<sup>0</sup> is called before or after the reduction receives the challenge ciphertext) in the RCCA-security game. Note that, when during a simulation of CheckDS, oracle GDec outputs replay, the reduction knows that a challenge coin was deposited, and uses this information to increase ctr.

### 6 Instantiation of the building blocks and efficiency

The instantiations we use are all proven secure in the standard model under non-interactive hardness assumptions.

Commitments and proofs. The commit-and-prove system C will be instantiated with Groth-Sahai proofs [\[GS08\]](#page-30-16), of which we use the instantiation based on SXDH (defined in Appendix [D\)](#page-67-0).

Theorem 13 ([\[GS08\]](#page-30-16)). The Groth-Sahai scheme, allowing to commit values from V := Z<sup>p</sup> ∪ G ∪ Gˆ is perfectly complete, perfectly sound and randomizable; it is (G ∪ Gˆ )-extractable, mode-indistinguishable assuming SXDH, and perfectly hiding in hiding mode.

We note that moreover, all our proofs can be made zero-knowledge [\[GS08\]](#page-30-16), and thus simulatable, because all pairing-product equations we use are homogeneous 

{28}------------------------------------------------

(i.e., the right-hand term is the neutral element). We have (efficient) extractability, as we only need to efficiently extract group elements from commitments (and no scalars) in our reductions. (Note that for information-theoretic arguments concerning soundness, Extr can also be inefficient.)

**Signature schemes.** For efficiency and type-compatibility reasons, we use two different signature schemes. The first one, S, must support the functionality SigCm, which imposes a specific format of messages. The second scheme, S', is less restrictive, which allows for more efficient instantiations. While all our other components rely on standard assumptions, we instantiate S with a scheme that relies on a non-interactive q-type assumption defined in  $[AFG^+10]$ .

**Theorem 14.** The signature scheme from  $[AFG^+10, Sect. 4]$  with message space  $\mathcal{M} := \{(g^m, \hat{g}^m) \mid m \in \mathbb{Z}_p\}$  is (strongly) unforgeable assuming q-ADHSDH and AWFCDH (see Appendix D), and it supports the SigCm functionality [Fuc11].

**Theorem 15.** The signature scheme from [AGHO11, Sect. 5] is structure-preserving with message space  $\mathcal{M}' := \hat{\mathbb{G}}$  and (strongly) unforgeable assuming SXDH.

Randomizable encryption schemes. To instantiate the RCCA-secure scheme  $\mathsf{E}'$  we follow the approach from Libert et al. [LPQ17]. Their construction is only for one group element, but by adapting the scheme, it can support encryption of a vector in  $\mathbb{G}^n$  for arbitrary n. In our e-cash scheme, we need to encrypt a vector in  $\mathbb{G}^2$ , and since it is not clear whether more recent efficient schemes like [FFHR19] can be adapted to this, we give an explicit construction, which we detail in Appendix B.2.

Recall that the RCCA-secure scheme E' is only used to encrypt the initial part of the serial number; using a less efficient scheme does thus not have a big impact on the efficiency of our scheme. From all other ciphertexts contained in a coin (which are under scheme E) we only require IACR security, which standard ElGamal encryption satisfies under DDH(!). Thus, we instantiate E with ElGamal vector encryption. (Note that our instantiation of E' is also built on top of ElGamal). We prove the following in the appendix.

<span id="page-28-1"></span>**Theorem 16.** Assuming SXDH, our randomizable encryption scheme in Appendix B.2 is RCCA-secure and the one in Appendix B.3 is IACR-secure.

**Double-spending tags.** We will use a scheme that builds on the one given in [BCFK15]. We have optimized the size of the tags and made explicit all the functionalities not given previously. We defer this to Appendix B.1.

#### <span id="page-28-0"></span>Efficiency analysis

We conclude by summarizing the sizes of objects in our scheme in the table below and refer to Appendix C for the details of our analysis.

For a group  $G \in \{\mathbb{G}, \mathbb{G}, \mathbb{Z}_p\}$ , let |G| denote the size of an element of G. Let  $c_{\text{btsrap}}$  denote the coin output by  $\mathcal{U}$  at the end of the Withdraw protocol (which corresponds to  $c_{\text{init}}$  plus secret values, like n,  $\rho_{sn}$ , etc., to be used when 

{29}------------------------------------------------

transferring the coin), and let cstd denote one (non-initial) component of the coin. After k transfers the size of a coin is |cbtsrap| + k|cstd|.

| pkB     | + 8 Gˆ  <br>15 G           | cbtstrap     | + 125 Gˆ  <br>6 Zp <br>+ 147 G |
| skU<br> | + 2 Gˆ  <br> Zp <br>+ 2 G  | cstd         | + 50 Gˆ  <br>54 G              |

{31}------------------------------------------------

### <span id="page-31-0"></span>A Security proofs

Some of our theorems in the appendix are more general than stated in the body of the paper: they also work for a scheme C that only satisfies computational soundness (whereas in the body we assumed perfect soundness).

### A.1 Unforgeability

**Theorem 17.** Suppose that there exists an adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  against unforgeability (Def. 2) of our transferable e-cash scheme with advantage  $\epsilon_{\text{unforg}}$  making at most d calls to oracle BDepo. Suppose that  $\mathcal{M}$  and the signature space of S are contained in  $\mathcal{V}'$ . Then we can build a polynomial-time adversary  $\mathcal{B}_1$  against the unforgeability of the signature scheme S with advantage  $\epsilon_{\text{sig}}$ , an adversary  $\mathcal{B}_2$  against the unforgeability of S' with advantage  $\epsilon'_{\text{sig}}$ , and  $\mathcal{B}_3$  and  $\mathcal{B}_4$  against the soundness of the commitment scheme S with advantage  $\epsilon_{h,1}$  and  $\epsilon_{h,2}$ . Then

$$\epsilon_{\text{unforg}} \le \epsilon_{h,1} + \epsilon_{h,2} + \epsilon_{\text{sig}} + \epsilon'_{\text{sig}} + \frac{d^2}{|\mathcal{N}|}.$$

**Proof.** Note that the adversary has two possibilities to win the game: either it creates a counterfeit (i.e.,  $q_W < |\mathcal{CL}|$ ), or it wins by making a deposit fail (i.e., CheckDS does neither output a list nor a valid pair with a registered user key). In our proof we will consider these two aspects separately. First we will prove in Proposition 18, that creating counterfeit is harder than breaking the unforgeability of S, or proving a false statement in C. In Proposition 19, we prove that if fresh nonces are picked during each deposits, then it is harder to make Deposit fail than breaking the unforgeability of S', or proving a false statement in C.

We first recall the unforgeability against the e-cash system:

```
\begin{aligned} \mathbf{Expt}^{\mathrm{unforg}}_{\mathcal{A}}(\lambda) &: \\ par \leftarrow \mathsf{ParamGen}(1^{\lambda}); \ (sk_{\mathcal{B}}, pk_{\mathcal{B}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{BKeyGen}(par) \\ \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{BRegist},\mathsf{BWith},\mathsf{BDepo}}(par, pk_{\mathcal{B}}) &: \\ \mathsf{If} \ \mathsf{in} \ \mathsf{a} \ \mathsf{BDepo} \ \mathsf{call}, \ \mathsf{CheckDS} \ \mathsf{does} \ \mathsf{not} \ \mathsf{return} \ \mathsf{a} \ \mathsf{coin} \ \mathsf{list} \\ \mathsf{Return} \ \mathsf{1} \ \mathsf{if} \ \mathsf{any} \ \mathsf{of} \ \mathsf{the} \ \mathsf{following} \ \mathsf{hold} \\ &- \mathsf{CheckDS} \ \mathsf{did} \ \mathsf{not} \ \mathsf{output} \ \mathsf{a} \ \mathsf{pair} \ (pk, \Pi) \\ &- \mathsf{VfyGuilt}(pk, \Pi) = 0 \\ &- pk \not\in \mathcal{UL} \\ \mathsf{Let} \ q_W \ \mathsf{be} \ \mathsf{the} \ \mathsf{number} \ \mathsf{of} \ \mathsf{calls} \ \mathsf{to} \ \mathsf{BWith} \\ \mathsf{If} \ q_W < |\mathcal{DCL}| \ \mathsf{then} \ \mathsf{return} \ \mathsf{1} \\ \mathsf{Return} \ \mathsf{0} &: \end{aligned}
```

and the unforgeability game against a signature scheme:

{32}------------------------------------------------

```
\begin{aligned} \mathbf{Expt}_{\mathsf{S},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{sig-uf}}(\lambda) & \text{Oracle: S.Sign}^*\left(sk,m,Q\right): \\ par \leftarrow \mathsf{S.Setup}\left(1^{\lambda}\right) & Q := Q \cup \{m\} \\ (sk,vk) \leftarrow \mathsf{S.KeyGen}\left(par\right) & \text{Return S.Sign}\left(sk,m\right) \\ Q := \emptyset & \\ (m,\sigma) \leftarrow \mathcal{B}^{\mathsf{S.Sign}^*\left(sk,\cdot,Q\right)}(par,vk) & \\ \text{Return}\left(m \not\in Q \land \mathsf{S.Verify}(vk,m,\sigma)\right) & \end{aligned}
```

Finally, the soundness of the commitment scheme:

```
\begin{split} \mathbf{Expt}^{\mathsf{soundness}}_{\mathsf{C},\mathcal{B}}(\lambda) &: \\ (ck,xk) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.ExSetup}(1^{\lambda}) \\ Q &:= \emptyset; \ (E,c_1,\ldots,c_n) \leftarrow \mathcal{B}(ck) \\ & \mathsf{Return} \ \left(\mathsf{C.Verify} \ (ck,E,c_1,\ldots,c_n) \ \land \ \neg E \ (\mathsf{C.Extr} \ (xk,c_1) \,,\ldots,\mathsf{C.Extr} \ (xk,c_n)) \,\right) \end{split}
```

Let  $E_{\rm unforg}$  be the event that  $\mathcal{A}$  wins the game, that is, at some point after a call to BDepo, CheckDS did not output a list, or  $q_W < |\mathcal{DCL}|$ . We partition  $E_{\rm unforg}$  as follows:

- $-E_{\text{Decrypt-fails}}$ : In CheckDS, a decryption fails or does not output any serial number and tag, when it is supposed to
- $E_{\text{same}}$ : In CheckDS, there is no j such that  $\vec{sn}_j \neq \vec{sn}'_j$
- $E_{\text{DDS-fails}}$ : In CheckDS, algorithm T.Detect does not output any  $(pk_{\mathsf{T}}, \Pi_G)$
- $E_{\text{incorrect}}$ : CheckDS outputs  $(pk_{i^*}, \Pi_G)$  such that VfyGuilt  $(pk_{i^*}, \Pi_G) = 0$
- $E_{\text{not-register}}$ :  $pk_{i^*} \notin \mathcal{UL}$
- $-E_{\text{counterfeit}}: q_W < |\mathcal{DCL}|$

We first build an adversary  $\mathcal{B}_1$  against the unforgeability of S, which will bet on  $E_{\text{counterfeit}}$ :  $q_W < |\mathcal{DCL}|$  (i.e.,  $\mathcal{A}$  creates valid money). Thus,  $\mathcal{A}$  has produced a committed signature for a fresh serial number and thus forged a signature for a fresh serial number or a false proof for the equation S.Verify (In this second case adversary  $\mathcal{B}_3$  will break soundness). Note that to simulate SigCm, adversary  $\mathcal{B}_1$  needs xk and SmSigCm.

```
Adversary \mathcal{B}_{1}^{\mathcal{A},\mathsf{S}.\mathsf{Sign}^{*}(sk,\cdot)} (par_{\mathsf{S}},vk):

Obtain Gr from par_{\mathsf{S}} (ck,xk) \leftarrow C.ExSetup (Gr)

par_{\mathsf{S}'} \leftarrow \mathsf{S}'.\mathsf{Setup} (Gr)

(sk',vk') \leftarrow S'.KeyGen (par_{\mathsf{S}'})

par_{\mathsf{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{Setup} (Gr)

par \leftarrow (1^{\lambda},Gr,par_{\mathsf{S}},par_{\mathsf{S}'},par_{\mathsf{T}},ck)

Coins<sub>D</sub> := \emptyset

Coins<sub>W</sub> := \emptyset

(ek,dk) \leftarrow E.KeyGen (Gr)

(ek',dk') \leftarrow E'.KeyGen (Gr)

pk_{\mathcal{B}} \leftarrow (ek',ek,vk,vk')

(sk_{\mathsf{T}},pk_{\mathsf{T}}) \leftarrow T.KeyGen(Gr)

sk_{\mathcal{D}} \leftarrow (\varepsilon,sk_{\mathsf{T}},pk_{\mathsf{T}})
```

{33}------------------------------------------------

```
Run \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{BRegist},\mathtt{BWith}^*,\mathtt{BDepo}}\left(par,pk_{\mathcal{B}}\right)
In each call of BWith, add the coin received to the list Coinsw
In each call of BDepo, add the coin received to the list Coins<sub>D</sub>
BWith* is similar to BWith, except instead of using SigCm, it uses SigCm*:
        \mathsf{SigCm}^*(c):
                m \leftarrow \mathsf{C.Extr}\left(xk,c\right)
                Use the oracle to obtain \Sigma \leftarrow \mathsf{S.Sign}^*(sk, m)
                (c_{\sigma}, \pi) \leftarrow \mathsf{SmSigCm}(xk, vk, c, \Sigma)
                Return (c_{\sigma}, \pi)
Let q_W be the number of successful calls to BWith
If q_W \geq |\mathcal{DCL}| then abort
Let D := \emptyset
Let W := \emptyset
For c \in \mathtt{Coins}_{\mathtt{W}}:
       Parse c as (c^0, (c^j)_{j=1}^i, n, sn, \rho_{sn}, \rho_{pk})
Parse c^0 as (c_{pk}^0, c_{cert}^0, \pi_{cert}^0, c_{sn}^0, \pi_{sn}^0, c_M, c_{\sigma}^0, \pi_{\sigma}^0, \tilde{c}_{sn}^0, \tilde{\pi}_{sn}^0)
        M := \mathsf{C.Extr}\left(xk, c_M\right)
        \sigma := \mathsf{C.Extr}\left(xk, c_{\sigma}^{0}\right)
        W := W \cup \{(M, \sigma)\}
For c \in \mathtt{Coins}_{\mathtt{D}}:
       Parse c as (c^0, (c^j)_{j=1}^i, n, sn, \rho_{sn}, \rho_{pk})
Parse c^0 as (c_{pk}^0, c_{cert}^0, \pi_{cert}^0, c_{sn}^0, \pi_{sn}^0, c_M, c_{\sigma}^0, \pi_{\sigma}^0, \tilde{c}_{sn}^0, \tilde{\pi}_{sn}^0)
        M := \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{Extr}\left(\hat{x}k, c_M\right)
        \sigma := \mathsf{C.Extr}\left(xk, c^0_\sigma\right)
        D := D \cup \{(M, \sigma)\}
If \exists (M, \sigma) \in W \setminus D:
        then return (M, \sigma)
Else abort
```

We let  $\varepsilon$  identify the part of the secret key that is ignored in the entire game (because the bank never spent a coin). By correctness of the committed signature of S, the simulation will be perfect. And by  $(\mathcal{M} \cup \mathcal{S})$ -extractability of C, we deduce that  $\mathcal{B}_1$  is efficient.

We now construct a first adversary  $\mathcal{B}_3$  against soundness:

```
Adversary \mathcal{B}_{3}^{\mathcal{A}}(ck):

Obtain Gr from ck

par_{S} \leftarrow S.Setup(Gr)

par_{S'} \leftarrow S'.Setup(Gr)

par_{T} \leftarrow T.Setup(Gr)

par \leftarrow (1^{\lambda}, Gr, par_{S}, par_{S'}, par_{T}, ck)

S := \emptyset

(pk_{\mathcal{B}} = (ek', ek, vk, vk'), sk_{\mathcal{W}} = (sk, sk'), sk_{\mathcal{D}}, sk_{\mathcal{CK}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{BKeyGen}()

Run \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{BRegist}, \mathsf{BWith}, \mathsf{BDepo}}(par, pk_{\mathcal{B}})

In each call of \mathsf{BDepo}, add the entire coin received in the list \mathsf{Coins}_{\mathsf{D}}

Let q_{\mathcal{W}} be the number of successful calls to \mathsf{BWith}
```

{34}------------------------------------------------

If 
$$q_W \geq |\mathcal{DCL}|$$
, then abort Let  $D := \emptyset$  For  $c \in \mathtt{Coins_D}$ :

Parse  $c$  as  $\left(c_0, (c_j)_{j=1}^i, n, sn, \rho_{sn}, \rho_{pk}\right)$ 

Add  $c_0$  to  $S$ 

Parse  $S$  as  $\left\{\left(c_{pk_{\mathsf{T}}}^i, c_{cert}^i, \pi_{cert}^i, c_{sn}^i, \pi_{sn}^i, c_M^i, c_\sigma^i, \pi_\sigma^i, \tilde{c}_{sn}^i, \tilde{\pi}_{sn}^i\right)\right\}_{1 \leq i \leq |S|}$ 

Parse  $\tilde{\pi}_{sn}^i$  as  $\left(c^i, \pi^i\right)$ 

Return  $\left(\bigwedge_{i=1}^{|S|} \left(\mathsf{E}'.\mathsf{Verify}\left(ek', X_1^i, X_2^i, \tilde{c}_{sn}^i\right) \wedge \mathsf{S}.\mathsf{Verify}\left(vk, X_3^i, X_4^i\right) = 1 \wedge \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{SVfy}_{init}\left(X_5^i, X_1^i, X_3^i\right)\right)$ ,  $c_{sn}^1, c_s^1, c_{sn}^1, c_{sn}^1, c_s^{|S|}, c_s^{|S|}, c_s^{|S|}, c_s^{|S|}, c_s^{|S|}, \sum_{i=1}^{|S|} \left(\pi^i \wedge \pi_\sigma^i \wedge \pi_{sn}^i\right)\right)$ 

<span id="page-34-0"></span>We define the following events:

 $E_{\text{sig}}$ :  $\mathcal{B}_1$  breaks the unforgeability of the signature scheme S; and  $E_{\text{com},1}$ :  $\mathcal{B}_3$  breaks the soundness of the commitment scheme C.

# **Proposition 18.** $E_{counterfeit} \subset E_{sig} \cup E_{com,1}$ .

Suppose that we are in case  $E_{\text{counterfeit}} \setminus E_{\text{sig}}$ . Because the coin has been accepted during Spend in a call to BDepo, the proofs output by  $\mathcal{B}_3$  are correct. Let  $(sn^1, \nu^1, M^1, pk_{\mathsf{T}}^1, \sigma^1, \ldots, sn^{|S|}, \nu^{|S|}, M^{|S|}, pk_{\mathsf{T}}^{|S|}, \sigma^{|S|})$  be the values that the challenger of the soundness game extracts from the commitments output by  $\mathcal{B}_3$ . If for some i: S.Verify  $(vk, M^i, \sigma^i) \neq 1$ , then  $\mathcal{B}_3$  wins the soundness game.

Suppose that  $\bigwedge_{i=1}^{|S|} \mathsf{S.Verify}\left(vk, M^i, \sigma^i\right) = 1$ . Since we are not in  $E_{\mathrm{sig}}$ , all values  $M^i$  correspond to coins that have been withdrawn. But there are only  $q_W$  such coins and thus  $q_W$  such messages M. Thus, we have  $\left|\left\{M^i\right\}_{i=1}^{|S|}\right| \leq q_W$ .

If  $\bigwedge_{i=1}^{|S|} \mathsf{T.SVfy}_{\mathrm{init}}\left(pk_{\mathsf{T}}^{i}, sn^{i}, M^{i}\right) \neq 1$ , then  $\mathcal{B}_{3}$  won the soundness game.

Assume  $\bigwedge_{i=1}^{|S|} \mathsf{T.SVfy}_{\mathrm{init}}\left(pk_\mathsf{T}^i, sn^i, M^i\right) = 1$ . Since  $\mathsf{T}$  is bootable, it must hold that  $\left|\left\{sn^i\right\}_{i=1}^{|S|}\right| \leq \left|\left\{M^i\right\}_{i=1}^{|S|}\right|$ , from which we get  $\left|\left\{sn^i\right\}_{i=1}^{|S|}\right| \leq q_W < |\mathcal{DCL}|$  (the last inequality follows since we assumed to be in  $E_{\mathrm{counterfeit}}$ ).

Note that by construction of  $\mathcal{DCL}$ , all the initial serial numbers of the elements of  $\mathcal{DCL}$  are different. Let us call this set I. From  $|I| = |\mathcal{DCL}|$ , we deduce  $|I| > |\{sn^i\}_{i=1}^{|S|}|$ . By construction,  $|I| = |\{E'.\mathsf{Dec}(dk', \tilde{c}_{sn}^i)\}_{i=1}^{|S|}|$ , and thus  $|\{E'.\mathsf{Dec}(dk', \tilde{c}_{sn}^i)\}_{i=1}^{|S|}| > |\{sn^i\}_{i=1}^{|S|}|$ . Let  $i_0$  be such that  $E'.\mathsf{Dec}(dk', \tilde{c}_{sn}^{i_0}) \notin |\{sn^i\}_{i=1}^{|S|}|$ . By correctness of E', we have  $E'.\mathsf{Enc}\left(pk, sn^{i_0}, \nu^{i_0}\right) \neq \tilde{c}_{sn}^{i_0}$ , and thus (again by correctness of E')  $E'.\mathsf{Verify}\left(pk, sn^{i_0}, \nu^{i_0}, \tilde{c}_{sn}^{i_0}\right) \neq 1$ .

We deduce that  $\bigwedge_{i=1}^{|S|} \mathsf{E}'.\mathsf{Verify}\left(pk,sn^i,\nu^i,\tilde{c}_{sn}^i\right) \neq 1$ , and consequently  $\mathcal{B}_3$  won the soundness game. We thus have  $E_{\mathrm{counterfeit}} \setminus E_{\mathrm{sig}} \subset E_{\mathrm{com},1}$ .

We build an algorithm to break unforgeability of  $\mathsf{S}'$ :

{35}------------------------------------------------

```
Adversary \mathcal{B}_{2}^{\mathcal{A},\mathsf{S}',\mathsf{Sign}^{*}(sk',\cdot)} (par_{\mathsf{S}'},vk'):
         Initialize \mathcal{UL} as empty list
         Obtain Gr from par_{S'}
         (ck, xk) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.ExSetup}(Gr)
         par_{\mathsf{S}} \leftarrow \mathsf{S.Setup}\left(Gr\right)
         (sk, vk) \leftarrow \mathsf{S.KeyGen}(Gr)
        par_{\mathsf{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{Setup}\left(Gr\right)
        par \leftarrow (1^{\lambda}, Gr, par_{S}, par_{S'}, par_{T}, ck)
         (ek', dk') \leftarrow \mathsf{E}'.\mathsf{KeyGen}(Gr)
         (ek, dk) \leftarrow \mathsf{E.KeyGen}\left(Gr\right)
         (sk_{\mathsf{T}}, pk_{\mathsf{T}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{KeyGen}\left(Gr\right)
         sk_{\mathcal{D}} \leftarrow (\varepsilon, pk_{\mathsf{T}}, sk_{\mathsf{T}})
        pk_{\mathcal{B}} \leftarrow (ek', ek, vk, vk')
Run \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{BRegist},\mathtt{BWith},\mathtt{BDepo}}(par, pk_{\mathcal{B}})
        Each time we would use S'.Sign in an oracle call we use
                  S'.Sign^*(sk',\cdot), and we add the input to \mathcal{UL}
         Let (pk, \Pi) be the output of the last call to BDepo
         If such a pair is never returned by BDepo, then abort
         Let c_1 be the last coin sent by the user
        Parse c_1 as (c^0, (c^j)_{j=1}^i, n, sn, \rho_{sn}, \rho_{pk})
        Let j be minimal such that (\vec{sn})_{j-1} \neq (\vec{sn'})_{j-1}
                  (using the notation from CheckDS)
        Parse c^{j-1} as \left(c_{pk_{\mathsf{T}}}^{j-1}, c_{cert}^{j-1}, \pi_{cert}^{j-1}, c_{sn}^{j-1}, \pi_{sn}^{j-1}, \underline{c_{tag}^{j-1}}, \underline{\pi_{tag}^{j-1}}, c_{M}, c_{\sigma}^{j-1}, \pi_{\sigma}^{j-1}, \right)
                                                                                                                         \tilde{c}_{\mathrm{sn}}^{j-1}, \tilde{\pi}_{\mathrm{sn}}^{j-1}, \tilde{c}_{\mathrm{tag}}^{j-1}, \tilde{\pi}_{\mathrm{tag}}^{j-1})
        \begin{aligned} pk_{\mathsf{T}} &:= \mathsf{C.Extr}\big(xk, c_{pk_{\mathsf{T}}}^{j-1}\big) \\ \sigma &:= \mathsf{C.Extr}\big(xk, c_{cert}^{j-1}\big) \end{aligned}
         If pk_{\mathsf{T}} \notin \mathcal{UL}:
                  then return (pk_{\mathsf{T}}, \sigma)
         Else abort
```

We denote by  $\varepsilon$  the part of the secret key that could be ignored in the protocols (e.g., the certificate *cert* of a receiver is never used). Let  $E'_{\text{sig}}$  be the event that  $\mathcal{B}_2$  breaks the unforgeability of  $\mathsf{S}'$ .

We construct a second adversary against soundness of C:

```
Adversary \mathcal{B}_{4}^{\mathcal{A}}(ck):
Obtain Gr from ck
par_{\mathsf{S}} \leftarrow \mathsf{S.Setup}(Gr) \; ; \; par_{\mathsf{S}'} \leftarrow \mathsf{S'.Setup}(Gr) \; ; \; par_{\mathsf{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{T.Setup}(Gr)
par \leftarrow \left(1^{\lambda}, Gr, par_{\mathsf{S}}, par_{\mathsf{S}'}, par_{\mathsf{T}}, ck\right)
\left(pk_{\mathcal{B}} = \left(ek', ek, vk, vk'\right), sk_{\mathcal{W}} = (sk, sk'), sk_{\mathcal{D}}, sk_{\mathcal{CK}}\right) \leftarrow \mathsf{BKeyGen}(\right)
\mathsf{Run} \; \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{BRegist}, \mathsf{BWith}, \mathsf{BDepo}}(par, pk_{\mathcal{B}})
\mathsf{Let} \; (pk, \Pi) \; \mathsf{be} \; \mathsf{the} \; \mathsf{output} \; \mathsf{of} \; \mathsf{the} \; \mathsf{last} \; \mathsf{call} \; \mathsf{to} \; \mathsf{BDepo}
\mathsf{If} \; \mathsf{such} \; \mathsf{a} \; \mathsf{pair} \; \mathsf{is} \; \mathsf{never} \; \mathsf{returned} \; \mathsf{by} \; \mathsf{BDepo}, \; \mathsf{then} \; \mathsf{abort}
\mathsf{Let} \; c \; \mathsf{be} \; \mathsf{the} \; \mathsf{last} \; \mathsf{coin} \; \mathsf{sent} \; \mathsf{by} \; \mathsf{the} \; \mathsf{user} \; \mathsf{and} \; i \; \mathsf{be} \; \mathsf{its} \; \mathsf{size}
```

{36}------------------------------------------------

```
Parse c as (c^0, (c^k)_{k=1}^i, n, \operatorname{sn}, \rho_{\operatorname{sn}}, \rho_{\operatorname{pk}})
   Let j be minimal such that (\vec{sn})_{i-1} \neq (\vec{sn'})_{i-1}
                                 (using the notation from CheckDS)
   Parse c^{(j-1)} as (c_{pk}^{(j-1)}, c_{cert}^{(j-1)}, \pi_{cert}^{(j-1)}, c_{sn}^{(j-1)}, \pi_{sn}^{(j-1)}, \underline{c_{tag}^{(j-1)}}, \underline{\pi_{tag}^{(j-1)}}, c_M,
                                                                                                                                                                                                                        c_{\sigma}^{(j-1)}, \pi_{\sigma}^{(j-1)}, \tilde{c}_{\text{sn}}^{(j-1)}, \tilde{\pi}_{\text{sn}}^{(j-1)}, \tilde{c}_{\text{tag}}^{(j-1)}, \tilde{\pi}_{\text{tag}}^{(j-1)})
   Do the same for all k \in \{0, ..., i\}
If j \neq 1, then parse \pi_{sn}^{(j-1)} as (\pi_{sn,\text{valid}}^{(j-1)}, c_{sn-pf}^{(j-1)})

Else (\pi_{sn,\text{valid}}^{(j-1)}, c_{sn-pf}^{(j-1)}) \leftarrow (\pi_{sn}^{(j-1)}, c_M)

Parse \pi_{sn}^j as (\pi_{sn,\text{valid}}^j, c_{sn-pf}^j) and \pi_{tag}^j as (\pi_{tag,\text{valid}}^j, c_{t-pf}^j)
  For all k \in \{0, ..., i\}:
Parse \tilde{\pi}_{sn}^k as (c_{\nu_{sn}}^k, \pi_{sn,eq}^k) and parse \tilde{\pi}_{tag}^k as (c_{\nu_{tag}}^k, \pi_{tag,eq}^k)
   Let c' be the coin that collides with c and i' be its size
Parse c' as (c'^0, (c'^k)_{k=1}^{i'}, n', sn', \rho'_{sn}, \rho'_{pk})
Parse c'^{(j-1)} as (c'^{(j-1)}_{pk}, c'^{(j-1)}_{cert}, \pi'^{(j-1)}_{cert}, c'^{(j-1)}_{sn}, \pi'^{(j-1)}_{sn}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, \underline{c'^{(j-1)}_{tag}}, {37}------------------------------------------------

where  $Y_j$  is the variable in the equations representing the purported values in the j-th commitment, and the  $X_i$ 's are the last 21 variables.

<span id="page-37-0"></span>We define the following two events:

 $E_{\text{com},2}$ :  $\mathcal{B}_4$  breaks the soundness of C, and

 $E_{\text{same-nonce}}$ : the same nonce is picked twice by the bank during two different calls to BDepo.

**Proposition 19.** 
$$E_{\text{unforg}} \setminus E_{\text{counterfeit}} \subset E_{\text{same}} \cup E_{\text{com},2} \cup E'_{\text{unforg}}$$
.

Suppose that we are in  $E_{\text{unforg}} \setminus (E_{\text{com},2} \cup E_{\text{counterfeit}} \cup E_{\text{same}})$ . Because the coin has been accepted, the proofs are correct (as they are verified in the Spend protocol, during a call to BDepo). We are thus in a case where the extracted commitment will verify the equations. Let

$$(sn^{0}, \dots, sn^{i}, tag^{1}, \dots, tag^{i}, pk_{tag}^{(j-1)}, cert^{(j-1)}, pk_{tag}^{j}, pk_{tag}^{\prime j}, sn^{(j-1)}, \nu_{sn}^{(j-1)}, sn^{\prime (j-1)}, v_{sn}^{\prime (j-1)}, sn^{\prime (j-1)}, v_{sn}^{\prime (j-1)}, sn^{-j}, v_{sn}^{\prime j}, v_{sn}^{\prime j}, sn^{\prime j}, v_{sn}^{\prime j}, sn^{\prime j}, v_{sn}^{\prime j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j}, sn^{-j},$$

be what the challenger of the soundness game extracts from the commitments output by  $\mathcal{B}_4$ . Since we are not in  $E_{\text{com},2}$  we have that  $\mathcal{B}_4$  loses the game: for all  $k \in \{1, \ldots, i\}$ :

E'. Verify 
$$(ek', sn^0, \nu_{sn}^0, \tilde{c}_{sn}^0) = \text{E.Verify}(ek, sn^k, \nu_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k) = 1,$$

and for all  $k \in \{1, \ldots, i\}$ :

E. Verify 
$$\left(ek, tag^k, \nu_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{tag}^k\right) = 1$$
.

By correctness of E and E', we deduce that  $E_{\text{Decrypt-fails}}$  will not happen. Being in  $E_{\text{unforg}} \setminus E_{\text{counterfeit}}$  means that CheckDS detected that the first SN-component of c is the same as that of another coin (here c'). Note that the last sn of a deposited coin is generated (with the key  $sk_{\text{T}}$ ) and encrypted by the bank itself. Now because we are not in  $E_{\text{same}}$ , we have that CheckDS will find some j, such that  $\vec{sn}_j \neq \vec{sn'}_j$ .

By construction, E.Dec  $(dk, \tilde{c}_{sn}^j)$  = E.Dec  $(dk, \tilde{c}_{sn}^{\prime j})$ , which by correctness of E (and because we are not in  $E_{\text{com, 2}}$ ) means  $sn^{(j-1)} = sn'^{(j-1)}$ . Since

$$\begin{split} 1 &= \mathsf{T.SVfy} \big( pk_{\mathsf{T}}^{j}, sn^{j}, sn\text{-}pf^{j} \big) \\ &= \mathsf{T.SVfy} \big( pk_{\mathsf{T}}^{\prime j}, sn^{\prime j}, sn\text{-}pf^{\prime j} \big) \\ &= \mathsf{T.TVfy} \big( pk_{\mathsf{T}}^{(j-1)}, sn^{(j-1)}, sn^{j}, tag^{j}, t\text{-}pf^{j} \big) \\ &= \mathsf{T.TVfy} \big( pk_{\mathsf{T}}^{\prime (j-1)}, sn^{(j-1)}, sn^{\prime j}, tag^{\prime j}, t\text{-}pf^{\prime j} \big) \\ &= \mathsf{T.SVfy}_{\mathrm{all}} \big( pk_{\mathsf{T}}^{(j-1)}, sn^{(j-1)}, sn\text{-}pf^{(j-1)} \big), \end{split}$$

and, because T is SN-identifiable, we get that  $pk_{tag}^{j} = pk_{tag}^{\prime j}$ .

Moreover, since T is two-extractable, we deduce that if  $pk_{tag}^j \in \mathcal{UL}$ , and that  $E_{\text{DDSfails}}$ ,  $E_{\text{incorrect}}$  and  $E_{\text{not-register}}$  will not happen.

{38}------------------------------------------------

We have proved that  $(E_{\text{unforg}} \setminus E_{\text{counterfeit}} \cup E_{\text{same}} \cup E_{\text{com}, 2}) \implies pk_{tag}^j \notin \mathcal{UL}$ . Finally note that if  $pk_{tag}^j \notin \mathcal{UL}$ , and if  $E_{\text{com}, 2} \cup E_{\text{same}} \cup E_{\text{counterfeit}}$  does not happen, then  $\mathcal{B}_2$  will win the unforgeability game against S'. This yields:

$$E_{\text{unforg}} \setminus (E_{\text{com},2} \cup E_{\text{counterfeit}}) \subset E_{\text{same}} \cup E'_{\text{sig}}.$$

Now suppose we are in  $E_{\text{same}}$ . By correctness of E, we deduce that the serial numbers were also identical before their encryption. Then by  $\mathcal{N}$ -injectivity, we have that the nonces picked during the deposits were the same, and we are therefore in  $E_{\text{same-nonce}}$ . Thus  $E_{\text{same}} \subset E_{\text{same-nonce}}$ . From this we deduce

$$E_{\text{unforg}} \subset E_{\text{com},2} \cup E_{\text{same-nonce}} \cup E'_{\text{sig}} \cup E_{\text{com},2} \cup E_{\text{sig}}.$$

By considering the probabilities, we finally conclude that

$$\epsilon \le \epsilon_{\mathrm{h},1} + \epsilon_{\mathrm{h},2} + \epsilon_{\mathrm{sig}} + \epsilon_{\mathrm{sig}}' + \frac{d^2}{N}.$$

#### A.2 Exculpability

<span id="page-38-0"></span>**Theorem 20.** Suppose there is an adversary A against exculpability (Def. 3) of our scheme with advantage  $\epsilon$  that makes at most u calls to the oracle URegist. Then there exist adversaries  $\mathcal{B}_1$  against tag-exculpability with advantage  $\epsilon_{\text{tag}}$ , and  $\mathcal{B}_2$  against mode-hiding of C with advantage  $\epsilon_{\text{m-ind}}$  such that

$$\epsilon \leq u \, \epsilon_{\text{tag}} + \epsilon_{\text{m-ind}}$$
.

We start with recalling the tag-exculpability game:

```
Experiment \mathbf{Expt}_{\mathsf{T},\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{tag-exculpability}}(Gr): par_{\mathsf{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{Setup}\,(Gr) (sk_{\mathsf{T}},pk_{\mathsf{T}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{KeyGen}\,(1^{\lambda}) (sk_{\mathsf{T}},pk_{\mathsf{T}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{KeyGen}\,(1^{\lambda}) (sn,sn\text{-}pf) \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{SGen}(sk,n) \mathsf{Return}\,\,sn \Pi' \leftarrow \mathcal{B}^{O_1(sk_{\mathsf{T}}),O_2(sk_{\mathsf{T}},\cdot)}\,(pk_{\mathsf{T}}) (pk_{\mathsf{T}}) \mathsf{Return}\,\,\mathsf{T}.\mathsf{VfyGuilt}\,(pk_{\mathsf{T}},\Pi') \mathsf{If}\,\,T[i] = \bot,\,\,\mathsf{abort}\,\,\mathsf{the}\,\,\mathsf{oracle}\,\,\mathsf{call}\,\,n := T[i]\,\,T[i] := \bot\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,\,
```

We construct the following adversary against tag-exculpability of T.

Adversary 
$$\mathcal{B}_{1}^{O_{1}(sk_{\mathsf{T}}),O_{2}(sk_{\mathsf{T}},\cdot)}$$
  $(par_{\mathsf{T}},pk_{\mathsf{T}})$ :

Obtain  $Gr$  from  $par_{\mathsf{T}}$ 
 $(ck,td) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmSetup}(Gr)$ 
 $par_{\mathsf{S}} \leftarrow \mathsf{S.Setup}(Gr)$ 
 $par_{\mathsf{S}'} \leftarrow \mathsf{S'.Setup}(Gr)$ 
 $par \leftarrow (1^{\lambda},par_{\mathsf{S}},par_{\mathsf{S}'},par_{\mathsf{T}},ck)$ 

{39}------------------------------------------------

```
pkB ← A (par)
u
 ∗ $←− {1, . . . , u}
(i
 ∗
  , Π∗
       ) ← AURegist,Spy,UWith,Rcv,Spd,S&R,UDepo (par, pkB)
In the u
        ∗
         -th call of URegist, use pkT (instead of running T.KeyGen)
If the adversary queries Spy (u
                                ∗
                                 ), abort
If the adversary queries UWith, Rcv, Spd, S&R, UDepo on u
                                                             ∗
                                                              ,
    use O1 and O2, and td (since skT is unknown)
If O2 fails, abort the entire procedure
Output Π∗
```

The game is perfectly simulated from A's point of view, except when it calls Spy(u ∗ ), or makes that user double-spend, or if it detects that we are in hidingmode (which happens with probability at most m-ind). Let Eex and Etag be the events that A wins and that B<sup>1</sup> wins, respectively. Suppose that we are in Eex. This means that A forges a proof against one of the registered users (and does not spy on her). The probability that this user is u ∗ is at least <sup>1</sup> u . In this case, we have:

- A did not spy on u <sup>∗</sup> or make her double-spend (as in both cases we would not be in Eex).
- VfyGuilt(pkT, Π<sup>∗</sup> ) = 1 (because we are in Eex); thus T.VfyGuilt(skT, Π<sup>∗</sup> ) = 1.

We thus deduce that

$$\Pr[E_{\mathrm{ex}}] \le u \Pr[E_{\mathrm{tag}}].$$

### <span id="page-39-0"></span>A.3 Coin anonymity

Theorem 21. Suppose there is an A against coin anonymity (c-an) of our scheme with advantage and let k be an upper-bound on the number of users transferring the challenge coins. Then there exist adversaries against modeindistinguishability of C and tag-anonymity of T with advantages m-ind and t-an, resp., such that

$$\epsilon \leq 2 \left( \epsilon_{\text{m-ind}} + (k+1)\epsilon_{\text{t-an}} \right).$$

Proof sketch. In the proof, we first define a hybrid game in which the commitment key is switched to hiding mode (hence the loss m-ind, which occurs twice for b = 0 and b = 1). All commitments are then perfectly hiding and the only information available to the adversary are the serial numbers and tags. (They are encrypted in the coin, but the adversary, impersonating the bank, can decrypt them.)

We then argue that, by tag anonymity of T, the adversary cannot link a user to a pair (sn,tag), even when it knows the users' secret keys. We define a sequence of k + 1 hybrid games (as k transfers involve k + 1 users); going through the user vector output by the adversary, we can switch, one by one, all users from the first two the second vector. Each switch can be detected by the adversary with probability at most 2t-an.

{40}------------------------------------------------

A technical difficulty occurs during the first swap: We would like to switch the two initial serial numbers of  $c_0$  and  $c_1$ , but this seems problematic, as during the first withdraw (of  $c_0$ ), the challenger does not yet know  $i_1$  (and possibly this user has not even been defined yet), and thus the initial serial number of  $c_1$ . But fortunately, we note (in Proposition 25) that in hiding mode of the proof system, we do not need to compute the initial serial numbers during the withdraws! This is because we only send to the adversary (playing the bank) committed elements and proofs that reveal no information. We can therefore compute theses serial numbers after these withdraws, and switch them at this later moment.

# Full proof. We recall $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0}^{\mathtt{c-an}}$ :

```
\begin{aligned} \mathbf{Expt}^{\mathtt{c-an}}_{\mathcal{A},0}(\lambda) \colon \\ par &\leftarrow \mathsf{ParamGen}(1^{\lambda}); \ pk_{\mathcal{B}} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(par) \\ i_{0} &\leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{URegist},\mathsf{Spy}} \\ \mathsf{Run} \ \mathsf{UWith}(i_{0}) \ \mathsf{with} \ \mathcal{A} \\ i_{1} &\leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{URegist},\mathsf{Spy}} \\ \mathsf{Run} \ \mathsf{UWith}(i_{1}) \ \mathsf{with} \ \mathcal{A} \\ &(i^{(\vec{0})}, i^{(\vec{1})}) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{URegist},\mathsf{Spy}} \\ \mathsf{Let} \ k := |i^{(\vec{0})}|; \ \text{if} \ k \neq |i^{(\vec{1})}|, \ \mathsf{abort} \ \mathsf{the} \ \mathsf{entire} \ \mathsf{procedure} \\ \mathsf{Then} \ \mathsf{repeat} \ \mathsf{the} \ \mathsf{following} \ \mathsf{step} \ \mathsf{for} \ j = 1, \ldots, k \colon \\ \mathsf{Run} \ \mathsf{S\&R}(2j-1, (i^{(\vec{0})})_{j}); \ \mathsf{Run} \ \mathsf{S\&R}(2j, (i^{(\vec{1})})_{j}) \\ \mathsf{Run} \ \mathsf{Spd}(2k+1+b) \ \mathsf{with} \ \mathcal{A} \\ \mathsf{Run} \ \mathsf{Spd}(2k+2-b) \ \mathsf{with} \ \mathcal{A} \\ b^* &\leftarrow \mathcal{A} \ ; \ \mathsf{return} \ b^* \end{aligned}
```

In the game  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{hiding}}^{\mathtt{c-an}}$ , we will change the commitment key. If the adversary detects this, it breaks the mode-indistinguishability of C. Thus the distribution of the experiment will not change except with probability  $\epsilon_{\mathrm{m-ind}}$  (Property 22).

```
Experiment \mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{hiding}}^{\mathrm{c-an}}(\lambda):

Gr \leftarrow \mathsf{GrGen}(1^{\lambda})
par_{\mathsf{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)
par_{\mathsf{S}} \leftarrow \mathsf{S}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)
(ck,td) \leftarrow \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{SmSetup}(Gr)
par \leftarrow \begin{bmatrix} (1^{\lambda},Gr,par_{\mathsf{S}},par_{\mathsf{S}'},par_{\mathsf{T}},ck) \end{bmatrix}
pk_{\mathcal{B}} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(par)
i_0 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{URegist},\mathsf{Spy}}
\mathsf{Run}\; \mathsf{UWith}(i_0)\; \mathsf{with}\; \mathcal{A}
i_1 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{URegist},\mathsf{Spy}}
\mathsf{Run}\; \mathsf{UWith}(i_1)\; \mathsf{with}\; \mathcal{A}
```

{41}------------------------------------------------

```
(i^{(\vec{0})}, i^{(\vec{1})}) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\text{URegist,Spy}}

Let k := |i^{(\vec{0})}|; if k \neq |i^{(\vec{1})}|, abort the entire procedure

Then repeat the following for j = 1, \dots, k:

Run S&R(2j - 1, (i^{(\vec{0})})_j); Run S&R(2j, (i^{(\vec{1})})_j)

Run Spd(2k + 1 + b) with \mathcal{A}

Run Spd(2k + 2 - b) with \mathcal{A}

b^* \leftarrow \mathcal{A}; return b^*
```

<span id="page-41-0"></span>**Proposition 22.** Expt<sup>c-an</sup><sub> $\mathcal{A},0$ </sub>( $\lambda$ ) and Expt<sup>c-an</sup><sub> $\mathcal{A},0,\text{hiding}$ </sub>( $\lambda$ ) are  $\epsilon_{\text{m-ind}}$ -statistically close.

Note that td is never used in  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{hiding}}^{\mathtt{c-an}}(\lambda)$ . Therefore, the game can be simulated using a mode-indistinguishability challenge (Gr,ck). If ck has been generated by C.Setup, this simulates  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{hiding}}^{\mathtt{c-an}}(\lambda)$ ; if ck has been generated by C.SmSetup, this simulates  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{hiding}}^{\mathtt{c-an}}$ . This experiment can therefore be seen as a mode-distinguisher.

Let  $C.SmPrv_{\rm sn}$ ,  $C.SmPrv_{\rm sn,init}$ ,  $C.SmPrv_{\rm tag}$ ,  $C.E.SmPrv_{\rm enc}$  denote analogs of algorithms  $C.Prv_{\rm sn}$ ,  $C.Prv_{\rm sn,init}$ ,  $C.Prv_{\rm tag}$ ,  $C.E.Prv_{\rm enc}$ , except that every C.Prv is substituted by C.SmPrv and every C.Cm by C.ZCm.

Now each time the challenger is using an oracle, it uses C.ZCm instead of C.Cm, C.SmPrv instead of C.Prv, C.SmPrvenc instead of C.Prvenc, etc.

Let  $S\&R_{ZK}$ ,  $UWith_{ZK}$ ,  $Spd_{ZK}$  denote these modified oracles.

```
Experiment \mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{ZK}}^{\mathtt{c-an}}(\lambda):
             Gr \leftarrow \mathsf{GrGen}(1^{\lambda})
             par_{\mathsf{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)
             par_{\mathsf{S}} \leftarrow \mathsf{S.Setup}(Gr)
             par_{\mathsf{S}'} \leftarrow \mathsf{S}'.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)
             (ck, td) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmSetup}(Gr)
             par \leftarrow (1^{\lambda}, Gr, par_{S}, par_{S'}, par_{T}, ck)
             pk_{\mathcal{B}} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(par)
             i_0 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist},\mathtt{Spy}}
             Run | UWith<sub>ZK</sub>(i_0) | with \mathcal{A}
             i_1 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist},\mathtt{Spy}}
             \operatorname{Run} \left| \mathtt{UWith}_{\mathrm{ZK}}(i_1) \right| \operatorname{with} \, \mathcal{A}
             (i^{(0)}, \overline{i^{(1)}}) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist},\mathtt{Spy}}
             Let k := |i^{(0)}|; if k \neq |i^{(1)}|, abort the entire procedure
             Then repeat the following step for j = 1, ..., k:
                          Run \left[ S\&R_{ZK} \right] (2j-1,(i^{(\vec{0})})_j); Run \left[ S\&R_{ZK} \right] (2j,(i^{(\vec{1})})_j)
             Run \boxed{\operatorname{Spd}_{\operatorname{ZK}}(2k+1+b)} with \mathcal{A}
             Run \boxed{\operatorname{Spd}_{\operatorname{ZK}}}(2k+2-b) with \mathcal{A}
             b^* \leftarrow \overline{\mathcal{A}}; return b^*
```

Because we are in the hiding mode, the following follows directly from *perfect* zero-knowledge in hiding mode:

{42}------------------------------------------------

**Proposition 23.**  $\operatorname{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\operatorname{hiding}}^{\operatorname{c-an}}(\lambda)$  and  $\operatorname{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\operatorname{ZK}}^{\operatorname{c-an}}(\lambda)$  are equivalently distributed.

We now consider the following part of  $\mathrm{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{ZK}}^{\mathtt{c-an}}(\lambda))$  in more detail:

```
i_0 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\texttt{URegist}, \texttt{Spy}}
Run UWith<sub>ZK</sub> (i_0) with \mathcal{A}
i_1 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\texttt{URegist}, \texttt{Spy}}
Run UWith<sub>ZK</sub>(i_1) with \mathcal{A}
```

We would like to swap the serial numbers of  $i_0$  and  $i_1$  by using tag-anonymity. The issue here is that in the first call to  $\mathsf{UWith}_{\mathsf{ZK}}$ , we do not know  $i_1$  yet (because it is only chosen in a second round). Fortunately, at this step we only sent  $\mathcal{A}$  data that is unrelated to this serial number, since we are using  $\mathsf{ZCm}$ . Thus, at the end of this part, we can compute the ciphertexts of both initial coins.

We can decompose this part of the game as follows:

```
\begin{split} &i_{0} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\text{IRegist}, \text{Spy}} \\ &n^{(0)} \overset{\$}{\rightleftharpoons} \mathcal{N}; \; \rho_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \rho_{\text{cert}}^{(0)}, \rho_{\text{pk}}^{(0)}, \rho_{M}^{(0)} \overset{\$}{\rightleftharpoons} \mathcal{R} \\ & (\text{sn}^{(0)}, M_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}) \leftarrow \text{T.SGen}_{\text{init}}(sk_{i_{0}}, n^{(0)}) \\ &c_{\text{cert}}^{(0)}, c_{\text{pk}}^{(0)}, c_{\text{pk}}^{(0)}, c_{\text{pk}}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{\text{cert}}^{(0)}, \rho_{\text{pk}}^{(0)}, \rho_{\text{pk}}^{(0)}, \rho_{\text{pk}}^{(0)}) \\ &\pi_{\text{cert}}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{C.SmPrv}(td, \text{S}'.\text{Verify}(vk', \cdot, \cdot) = 1, \rho_{\text{pk}}^{(0)}, \rho_{\text{cert}}^{(0)}) \\ &\pi_{\text{sn}}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{C.SmPrv}_{\text{sn,init}}(td, \rho_{\text{pk}}^{(0)}, \rho_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \rho_{\text{M}}^{(0)}) \\ &\text{Send} \; (c_{pk}^{(0)}, c_{\text{cert}}^{(0)}, \pi_{\text{cert}}^{(0)}, e_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, c_{\text{M}}^{(0)}, \pi_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}) \; \text{to} \; A \\ &\text{Receive} \; (c_{\sigma}^{(0)}, \pi_{\sigma}^{(0)}) \; \text{from} \; \mathcal{A} \\ &\text{Receive} \; (c_{\sigma}^{(0)}, \pi_{\sigma}^{(0)}) \; \text{from} \; \mathcal{A} \\ &\text{If C.Verify}(ck, \text{S.Verify}(vk, \cdot, \cdot) = 1, c_{M}^{(0)}, c_{\sigma}^{(0)}, \pi_{\sigma}) = 0, \; \text{then return} \; \bot \\ &v_{\text{sn}}^{(0)} \overset{\$}{\rightleftharpoons} \mathcal{R} \\ &\tilde{c}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{E.Enc}(ek, \text{sn}^{(0)}, \nu_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}) \\ &\tilde{\pi}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{C.SmPrv}_{\text{enc}}(td, ek, \rho_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \tilde{c}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}) \\ &\tilde{\pi}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{C.SmPrv}_{\text{enct}}(td, ek, \rho_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \tilde{c}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}) \\ &\tilde{\pi}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{C.SmPrv}_{\text{enct}}(td, ek, \rho_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \pi_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \tilde{c}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \tilde{c}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}), \\ &\tilde{\pi}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{C.SmPrv}_{\text{enct}}(td, ek, \rho_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \tilde{c}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \tilde{c}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \tilde{c}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \tilde{c}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \tilde{c}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}), \\ &\rho_{\text{sn}}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{C.SmPrv}_{\text{sn}}(th, c_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \sigma_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \tilde{c}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \tilde{c}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \tilde{c}_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}), \\ &\tilde{\pi}_{\text{sn}}^{(1)} \leftarrow \text{C.SmPrv}_{\text{sn}}(td, c_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}, c_{
```

{43}------------------------------------------------

$$\begin{split} \tilde{c}_{sn}^{(1)} \leftarrow \text{E.Enc}(ek, sn^{(1)}, \nu_{sn}^{(1)}) \\ \tilde{\pi}_{sn}^{(1)} \leftarrow \text{C.SmPrv}_{\text{enc}}(td, ek, \rho_{sn}^{(1)}, \tilde{c}_{sn}^{(1)}) \\ \text{Pick } \rho^{(1)\prime} \text{ long enough to compute the following:} \\ c_{1}^{(1)} = \left( \text{Rand}((c_{pk}^{(1)}, c_{cert}^{(1)}, \pi_{cert}^{(1)}, c_{sn}^{(1)}, \pi_{sn}^{(1)}, c_{M}^{(1)}, c_{\sigma}^{(1)}, \pi_{\sigma}^{(1)}, \tilde{c}_{sn}^{(1)}, \tilde{\pi}_{sn}^{(1)}), \rho^{(\vec{1})\prime} \right), \\ n^{(1)}, sn^{(1)}, \rho_{sn}^{(1)} + (\rho^{(\vec{1})\prime})_{sn}, \rho_{pk}^{(1)} + (\rho^{(\vec{1})\prime})_{pk} \right) \\ \mathcal{CL}[2] \leftarrow (i_{1}, c_{1}^{(1)}, 0, \mathcal{A}) \end{split}$$

We can do the sn-computations and the encryptions at the end of this part (because they are not related to data sent to  $\mathcal{A}$ ). We can therefore replace the previous instructions by the following algorithm DoubleUWith:

### ${\tt DoubleUWith}^{\mathcal{A}} \colon$

```
\begin{split} i_{0} &\leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\text{URegist,Spy}} \\ \rho_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \rho_{\text{cert}}^{(0)}, \rho_{pk}^{(0)}, \rho_{M}^{(0)} &\stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{R}; \text{ Compute:} \\ c_{\text{cert}}^{(0)}, c_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, c_{pk}^{(0)}, c_{M}^{(0)} &\leftarrow \text{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{\text{cert}}^{(0)}, \rho_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \rho_{pk}^{(0)}, \rho_{M}^{(0)}) \end{split}
\pi_{cert}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{C.SmPrv}(td, S'.\text{Verify}(vk', \cdot, \cdot) = 1, \rho_{pk}^{(0)}, \rho_{cert}^{(0)})
\pi_{sn}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{C.SmPrv}_{sn, \text{init}}(td, \rho_{pk}^{(0)}, \rho_{sn}^{(0)}, \rho_{M}^{(0)})
Send (c_{pk}^{(0)}, c_{cert}^{(0)}, \pi_{cert}^{(0)}, c_{sn}^{(0)}, c_{M}^{(0)}, \pi_{sn}^{(0)}) to \mathcal{A}
Receive (c_{\sigma}^{(0)}, \pi_{\sigma}^{(0)}) from \mathcal{A}
 If \mathsf{C.Verify}(ck,\mathsf{S.Verify}(vk,\cdot,\cdot)=1,c_M^{(0)},c_\sigma^{(0)},\pi_\sigma)=0 then output \perp i_1 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist},\mathtt{Spy}}
  \rho_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}, \rho_{\text{cert}}^{(1)}, \rho_{pk}^{(1)}, \rho_{M}^{(1)} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{R}; \text{ Compute:}
                         c_{pk}^{(1)} \leftarrow \text{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{pk}^{(1)}) \; ; \; c_{cert}^{(1)} \leftarrow \text{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{cert}^{(1)}) \\ c_{sn}^{(1)} \leftarrow \text{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{sn}^{(1)}) \; ; \; c_{M}^{(1)} \leftarrow \text{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{M}^{(1)})
\pi_{cert}^{(1)} \leftarrow \text{C.SmPrv}(td, S'. \text{Verify}(vk', \cdot, \cdot) = 1, \rho_{pk}^{(1)}, \rho_{cert}^{(1)})
\pi_{sn}^{(1)} \leftarrow \text{C.SmPrv}_{sn, \text{init}}(td, \rho_{pk}^{(1)}, \rho_{sn}^{(1)}, \rho_{M}^{(1)})
\text{Send } (c_{pk}^{(1)}, c_{cert}^{(1)}, \pi_{cert}^{(1)}, c_{sn}^{(1)}, c_{M}^{(1)}, \pi_{sn}^{(1)}) \text{ to } \mathcal{A}
\text{Receive } (c_{\sigma}^{(1)}, \pi_{\sigma}^{(1)}) \text{ from } \mathcal{A}
 If C.Verify(ck, \mathsf{S.Verify}(vk, \cdot, \cdot) = 1, c_M^{(1)}, c_\sigma^{(1)}, \pi_\sigma^{(1)}) = 0 then output \bot
  n^{(0)}, n^{(1)} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{N}; (sn^{(0)}, M_{sn}^{(0)}) \leftarrow \mathsf{T.SGen}_{init}(sk_{i_0}, n^{(0)})
  (sn^{(1)}, M_{sn}^{(1)}) \leftarrow \mathsf{T.SGen}_{init}(sk_{i_1}, n^{(1)})
  \nu_{\rm sn}^{(0)}, \nu_{\rm sn}^{(1)} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{R}
  \tilde{c}_{sn}^{(0)} \leftarrow \mathsf{E.Enc}(ek,sn^{(0)},\nu_{sn}^{(0)}); \ \tilde{c}_{sn}^{(1)} \leftarrow \mathsf{E.Enc}(ek,sn^{(1)},\nu_{sn}^{(1)})
  \tilde{\pi}_{sn}^{(0)} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmPrv}_{enc}(td, ek, \rho_{sn}^{(0)}, \tilde{c}_{sn}^{(0)})
  \tilde{\pi}_{\mathrm{sn}}^{(1)} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmPrv}_{\mathrm{enc}}(td, ek, \rho_{\mathrm{sn}}^{(1)}, \tilde{c}_{\mathrm{sn}}^{(1)})
  Pick uniformly at random \rho^{(\vec{0})\prime}, \rho^{(\vec{1})\prime} long enough to compute:
  c_1^{(0)} = \big(\mathsf{Rand}((c_{pk}^{(0)}, c_{cert}^{(0)}, \pi_{cert}^{(0)}, c_{sn}^{(0)}, \pi_{sn}^{(0)}, c_M^{(0)}, c_\sigma^{(0)}, \pi_\sigma^{(0)}, \tilde{c}_{sn}^{(0)}, \tilde{\pi}_{sn}^{(0)}), \rho^{(\vec{0})\prime}),
 n^{(0)}, sn^{(0)}, \rho_{sn}^{(0)} + (\rho^{(\vec{0})\prime})_{sn}, \rho_{pk}^{(0)} + (\rho^{(\vec{0})\prime})_{pk}) c_1^{(1)} = \left( \mathsf{Rand}((c_{pk}^{(1)}, c_{cert}^{(1)}, \pi_{cert}^{(1)}, c_{sn}^{(1)}, \pi_{sn}^{(1)}, c_M^{(1)}, c_{\sigma}^{(1)}, \pi_{\sigma}^{(1)}, \tilde{c}_{sn}^{(1)}, \tilde{\pi}_{sn}^{(1)}), \rho^{(\vec{1})\prime} \right),
                                                                                                                               n^{(1)}, \operatorname{sn}^{(1)}, \rho_{\operatorname{sn}}^{(1)} + (\rho^{(1)\prime})_{\operatorname{sn}}, \rho_{\operatorname{pk}}^{(1)} + (\rho^{(1)\prime})_{\operatorname{pk}}
```

$$\mathcal{CL}[1] \leftarrow (i_0, c_1^{(0)}, 0, \mathcal{A}) \; ; \; \mathcal{CL}[2] \leftarrow (i_1, c_1^{(1)}, 0, \mathcal{A})$$
  
Return  $(i_0, i_1)$ 

To express these instruction changes, we define the following game.

```
Experiment \mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{ZKV2}}^{\mathsf{c-an}}(\lambda):

Gr \leftarrow \mathsf{GrGen}(1^{\lambda})

par_\mathsf{T} \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)

par_\mathsf{S} \leftarrow \mathsf{S}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)

par_\mathsf{S'} \leftarrow \mathsf{S'}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)

(ck,td) \leftarrow \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{SmSetup}(Gr)

par \leftarrow (1^{\lambda},par_\mathsf{S},par_{\mathsf{S'}},par_{\mathsf{T}},ck)

pk_{\mathcal{B}} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(par)

(i_0,i_1) \leftarrow \mathsf{DoubleUWith}^{\mathcal{A}}

(i^{(0)},i^{(1)}) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{URegist},\mathsf{Spy}}

Let k:=|i^{(0)}|; \text{ if } k \neq |i^{(1)}|, \text{ abort the entire procedure}

Then repeat the following for j=1,\ldots,k:

Run \mathsf{S\&R_{ZK}}(2j-1,(i^{(0)})_j,); \mathsf{Run} \, \mathsf{S\&R_{ZK}}(2j,(i^{(1)})_j)

Run \mathsf{Spd_{ZK}}(2k+1+b) with \mathcal{A}

Run \mathsf{Spd_{ZK}}(2k+2-b) with \mathcal{A}

b^* \leftarrow \mathcal{A}; \mathsf{return} \, b^*
```

Since this change is transparent for the adversary, we get the following:

**Proposition 24.** Expt<sup>c-an</sup><sub>A,0,ZK</sub>( $\lambda$ ) and Expt<sup>c-an</sup><sub>A,0,ZKV2</sub>( $\lambda$ ) are equally distributed.

Next we have to swap the serial numbers. We define two new procedures:

```
\begin{aligned} & \text{DoubleUWith}_{\text{rev}}^{\mathcal{A}} \colon \\ & i_0 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\text{URegist}, \text{Spy}} \\ & \rho_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \rho_{\text{cert}}^{(0)}, \rho_{pk}^{(0)}, \rho_{M}^{(0)} \stackrel{\$}{\Leftarrow} \mathcal{R}; \text{ Compute:} \\ & c_{\text{cert}}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{\text{cert}}^{(0)}) \\ & c_{\text{sn}}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}); c_{pk}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{pk}^{(0)}) \\ & c_{M}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{M}^{(0)}) \\ & \pi_{\text{cert}}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{C.SmPrv}(td, \text{S}'.\text{Verify}(vk', \cdot, \cdot) = 1, \rho_{pk}^{(0)}, \rho_{\text{cert}}^{(0)}) \\ & \pi_{\text{sn}}^{(0)} \leftarrow \text{C.SmPrv}_{\text{sn,init}}(td, \rho_{pk}^{(0)}, \rho_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}, \rho_{M}^{(0)}) \\ & \text{Send} \ (c_{pk}^{(0)}, c_{\text{cert}}^{(0)}, \pi_{\text{cert}}^{(0)}, c_{m}^{(0)}, \sigma_{M}^{(0)}, \pi_{\text{sn}}^{(0)}) \text{ to } \mathcal{A} \\ & \text{Receive} \ (c_{\sigma}^{(0)}, \pi_{\sigma}^{(0)}) \text{ from } \mathcal{A} \\ & \text{If C.Verify}(ck, \text{S.Verify}(vk, \cdot, \cdot) = 1, c_{M}^{(0)}, c_{\sigma}^{(0)}, \pi_{\sigma}) = 0 \text{ then output } \bot \\ & i_1 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\text{URegist}, \text{Spy}} \\ & \rho_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}, \rho_{\text{cert}}^{(1)}, \rho_{pk}^{(1)}, \rho_{M}^{(1)} \stackrel{\$}{\Leftarrow} \mathcal{R}; \text{ Compute:} \\ & c_{\text{cert}}^{(1)} \leftarrow \text{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{\text{cert}}^{(1)}) \\ & c_{\text{sn}}^{(1)} \leftarrow \text{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{\text{sn}}^{(1)}) \end{aligned}
```
