{46}------------------------------------------------

```
\begin{split} \text{T.Verify}(ck, c_{pk}^i, c_{sn}', c_{tag}, \pi_{tag}) & \wedge \text{C.Verify}_{\text{enc}}(ck, ek, c_{tag}, \tilde{c}_{tag}, \tilde{\pi}_{tag}), \\ & \text{if any of them rejects then output } \bot \\ \text{Else choose a sufficiently long vector of randomness } \vec{\rho''} \text{ to compute:} \\ c'' &\leftarrow \text{Rand}\left((c^0, (c^j)_{j=1}^i, c_{pk}', c_{cert}', \pi_{cert}', c_{sn}', \pi_{sn}', c_{tag}, \pi_{tag}, \tilde{c}_{sn}', \tilde{\pi}_{sn}', \tilde{c}_{tag}', \tilde{\pi}_{tag}'), \vec{\rho''}\right) \\ c_{\text{new}} &:= \left(c'', n', \text{sn}', \rho_{sn}' + (\vec{\rho''})_{\text{sn}'}, \rho_{pk}' + (\vec{\rho''})_{pk'}\right) \\ \mathcal{CL}[|\mathcal{CL}| + 1] &:= (i, c_{\text{new}}, 0, j) \end{split}
```

We define a new game for all  $l \in \{0, ..., k-1\}$ :

```
Experiment \mathbf{Expt}^{\mathtt{c-an}}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{ZKV2},l}(\lambda):
          Gr \leftarrow \mathsf{GrGen}(1^{\lambda})
           par_{\mathsf{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)
           par_{\mathsf{S}} \leftarrow \mathsf{S.Setup}(Gr)
           par_{\mathsf{S}'} \leftarrow \mathsf{S}'.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)
           (ck, td) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmSetup}(Gr)
           par \leftarrow (1^{\lambda}, par_{S}, par_{S'}, par_{T}, ck)
           pk_{\mathcal{B}} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(par)
           (i_0, i_1) \leftarrow \text{DoubleUWith}_{\text{rev}}^{\mathcal{A}} \ (i_0, i_1) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\text{URegist,Spy}}
           Let k := |i^{(0)}|; if k \neq |i^{(1)}|, abort the entire procedure
            Consider i_0 as (i^{(0)})_0, and i_1 as (i^{(1)})_0
            For all b, j : sk_j^{(b)} \leftarrow \overline{\mathcal{UL}[(i^{(\vec{b})})_j].sk}
           Repeat the following for j = 1, ..., l:
                        Run S&R<sub>ZK,inv</sub> (2j-1,(i^{(0)})_j,sk_{i-1}^{(1)},sk_i^{(1)})
                         Run S&R<sub>ZK,inv</sub> (2j, (\vec{i^{(1)}})_j, sk_{j-1}^{(0)}, sk_j^{(0)})
            Run S\&R_{ZK,inv} (2l+1,(i^{(0)})_{l+1},sk_l^{(1)},sk_{l+1}^{(0)})
            Run S&R<sub>ZK,inv</sub> (2l+2,(i^{(1)})_{l+1},sk_l^{(0)},sk_{l+1}^{(1)})
           Repeat the following for j = l + 2, \dots, k:
                      Run S&R<sub>ZK</sub> (2j-1,(i^{(0)})_j); Run S&R<sub>ZK</sub> (2j,(i^{(1)})_j)
           Run \operatorname{Spd}_{\operatorname{ZK}}(2k+1+b) with \mathcal A
           Run \operatorname{Spd}_{\operatorname{ZK}}(2k+2-b) with \mathcal A
           b^* \leftarrow \mathcal{A}; return b^*
```

<span id="page-46-0"></span>**Proposition 25.** Expt<sup>c-an</sup><sub> $\mathcal{A},0,ZKV2$ </sub>( $\lambda$ ) and Expt<sup>c-an</sup><sub> $\mathcal{A},0,ZKV2,0$ </sub>( $\lambda$ ) are  $2\epsilon_{t-an}$ -statistically close.

We receive a challenge  $par_{\mathsf{T}}$  in the tag-anon game for T (and not the tag exculpability game, in contrast to the proof of Theorem 20), and we use  $par_{\mathsf{T}}$  as parameter for the tags instead of generating it in  $\mathrm{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{ZKV2}}^{\mathrm{c-an}}$ .

{47}------------------------------------------------

In DoubleUWith, we send to the tag-anon-challenger the secret keys of  $i_0$  and  $i_1$ , and we use  $O_1$  to generate the serial number of  $i_0$  in DoubleUWith and  $O_2(0)$  to generate the corresponding tag in the first  $S\&R_{ZK}^4$ .

If the challenger was in mode 0, this will not change the experiment. But if the challenger was in mode 1, it will replace  $i_0$  by  $i_1$ . Let  $\operatorname{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\operatorname{ZKV2},-1}^{\operatorname{c-an}}$  denote the game corresponding to this swap and  $\Delta$  be the statistical distance.

We have just proved that

$$\Delta\left(\operatorname{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{ZKV2}}^{\mathrm{c-an}}(\lambda),\operatorname{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{ZKV2},-1}^{\mathrm{c-an}}(\lambda)\right) \leq \epsilon_{\mathrm{t-an}}.$$

Analogously, we replace  $i_1$  by  $i_0$ , i.e., we show that

$$\Delta(\operatorname{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\operatorname{ZKV2},-1}^{\operatorname{c-an}}(\lambda),\operatorname{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\operatorname{ZKV2},0}^{\operatorname{c-an}}(\lambda)) \leq \epsilon_{\operatorname{t-an}},$$

and therefore 
$$\Delta(\text{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\text{ZKV2}}^{\text{c-an}}(\lambda), \text{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\text{ZKV2},0}^{\text{c-an}}(\lambda)) \leq 2\epsilon_{\text{t-an}}.$$

The proof is completely analogous for the following property, which lets us swap multiple games.

**Proposition 26.** For all  $l \in \{0, ..., k-2\}$ , we have that  $\operatorname{Expt}_{\mathcal{A}, 0, \operatorname{ZKV2}, l}^{\operatorname{c-an}}(\lambda)$  and  $\operatorname{Expt}_{\mathcal{A}, 0, \operatorname{ZKV2}, l+1}^{\operatorname{c-an}}(\lambda)$  are  $2\epsilon_{\operatorname{t-an}}$ -statistically close.

Finally, we define a last oracle to swap the last keys (and the corresponding game):

```
Spd_{ZK,inv}(k,sk_1):
              Receive (sn', \rho'_{sn}) from \mathcal{A}
              c \leftarrow \mathcal{CL}|k|.c
             Parse c as (c^0, (c^j = (c^j_{pk}, c^j_{cert}, \pi^j_{cert}, c^j_{sn}, \pi^j_{sn}, c^j_{tag}, \pi^j_{tag}, \tilde{c}^j_{sn}, \tilde{c}^j_{tag}, \tilde{\pi}^j_{sn}, \tilde{\pi}^j_{tag}))_{i=1}^i,
                                                                                                                                                                 n, \mathrm{sn}, \rho_{\mathrm{sn}}, \rho_{\mathrm{pk}}

\rho_{tag}, \nu_{tag}, \rho_{t\text{-}pf} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{R}

              (tag, t\text{-}pf) \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{Gen}(par_{\mathsf{T}}, sk_1, n, sn')
              c_{tag} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{tag})
              \tilde{c}_{tag} \leftarrow \mathsf{E.Enc}(ek, tag, \nu_{tag})
              \pi_{tag} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmPrv}_{tag}(td, pk_{tag}, sn, sn', tag, t\text{-}pf, \rho_{pk}, \rho_{sn}, \rho'_{sn}, \rho_{tag}, \rho_{t\text{-}pf})
              \tilde{\pi}_{tag} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmPrv}_{enc}(td, ek, \tilde{\rho}_{tag}, \tilde{c}_{tag})
              Send (c^0, (c^j)_{j=1}^i, c_{tag}, \pi_{tag}, \tilde{c}_{tag}, \tilde{\pi}_{tag}) to \mathcal{A}
Experiment \mathbf{Expt}^{\mathtt{c-an}}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{ZKV2},k}(\lambda):
              Gr \leftarrow \mathsf{GrGen}(1^{\lambda})
              par_{\mathsf{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)
              par_{\mathsf{S}} \leftarrow \mathsf{S.Setup}(Gr)
              par_{\mathsf{S}'} \leftarrow \mathsf{S}'.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)
              (ck, td) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmSetup}(Gr)
```

<span id="page-47-0"></span>We use the oracle only in these step; for the other serial number and tag generations, we use the secret keys (which we have generated) like in  $\text{Expt}_{\mathcal{A}.0,\text{ZKV2}}^{\text{c-an}}$ .

{48}------------------------------------------------

$$\begin{aligned} & par \leftarrow (1^{\lambda}, par_{\mathsf{S}}, par_{\mathsf{S}'}, par_{\mathsf{T}}, ck) \\ & pk_{\mathcal{B}} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(par) \\ & (i_0, i_1) \leftarrow \mathsf{DoubleUWith}_{\mathsf{rev}}^{\mathcal{A}} \\ & (i^{(\vec{0})}, i^{(\vec{1})}) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{URegist}, \mathsf{Spy}} \\ & \mathsf{Let} \ k := |i^{(\vec{0})}|; \ \text{if} \ k \neq |i^{(\vec{1})}|, \ \text{abort the entire procedure} \\ & \mathsf{Consider} \ i_0 \ \text{as} \ (i^{(\vec{0})})_0, \ \text{and} \ i_1 \ \text{as} \ (i^{(\vec{1})})_0 \\ & \mathsf{For} \ \text{all} \ \ b, j : sk_j^{(b)} \leftarrow \mathcal{UL}[(i^{(\vec{b})})_j].sk \\ & \mathsf{Then \ repeat \ the \ following \ for} \ j = 1, \dots, \boxed{k}: \\ & \mathsf{Run} \ \mathsf{S\&R}_{\mathsf{ZK,inv}} \ (2j-1, (i^{(\vec{0})})_j, \mathcal{UL}[(i^{(\vec{1})})_{j-1}].sk, \mathcal{UL}[(i^{(\vec{1})})_j].sk) \\ & \mathsf{Run} \ \mathsf{S\&R}_{\mathsf{ZK,inv}} \ (2j, (i^{(\vec{1})})_j, \mathcal{UL}[(i^{(\vec{0})})_{j-1}].sk, \mathcal{UL}[(i^{(\vec{0})})_j].sk) \\ & \mathsf{Run} \ \mathsf{Spd}_{\mathsf{ZK,inv}} \ (2k+1+b, \mathcal{UL}[(i^{(\vec{0})})_k].sk) \ \text{with} \ \mathcal{A} \\ & \mathsf{Run} \ \mathsf{Spd}_{\mathsf{ZK,inv}} \ (2k+2-b, \mathcal{UL}[(i^{(\vec{0})})_k].sk) \ \text{with} \ \mathcal{A} \\ & \mathsf{Run} \ \mathsf{Spd}_{\mathsf{ZK,inv}} \ (2k+2-b, \mathcal{UL}[(i^{(\vec{0})})_k].sk) \ \text{with} \ \mathcal{A} \\ & \mathsf{Run} \ \mathsf{Spd}_{\mathsf{ZK,inv}} \ (2k+2-b, \mathcal{UL}[(i^{(\vec{0})})_k].sk) \ \text{with} \ \mathcal{A} \end{aligned}$$

Analogously to previous two propositions, we get:

**Proposition 27.** Expt<sup>c-an</sup><sub> $\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{ZKV2},k-1$ </sub>( $\lambda$ ) and Expt<sup>c-an</sup><sub> $\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{ZKV2},k$ </sub>( $\lambda$ ) are  $2\epsilon_{\text{t-an}}$ -statistically close.

By noting that two randomized commitments of the same type in the hiding-mode have the (exact) same distribution, we get that  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{ZKV2},k}^{\mathtt{c-an}}(\lambda)$  is equally distributed as  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},1,\mathrm{ZK}}^{\mathtt{c-an}}(\lambda)$ .

From a similar reasoning, we get that  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},1,\mathrm{ZK}}^{\mathtt{c-an}}(\lambda)$  is  $\epsilon_{\mathrm{m-ind}}$  statistically close to  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},1}^{\mathtt{c-an}}(\lambda)$ . Finally, we deduce that  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},1}^{\mathtt{c-an}}(\lambda)$  is  $2(\epsilon_{\mathrm{ZK}}+(k+1)\epsilon_{\mathrm{t-an}})$ -statistically-close to  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0}^{\mathtt{c-an}}(\lambda)$ .

Note that  $\epsilon_{t-an}$  is the advantage against tag-anonymity of an adversary that is making just one call to  $O_1$  and one to  $O_2$ .

#### A.4 Coin transparency

**Theorem 28.** Let A be an adversary against **coin-transparency** (c-tr) of our scheme with advantage  $\epsilon$ , and let  $\ell$  be the size of the challenge coins, and k be an upper-bound on the number of users transferring the challenge coins. Then there exist adversaries against mode-indistinguishability of C, tag-anonymity of T, IACR-security of E and RCCA-security of E' with advantages  $\epsilon_{\text{m-ind}}$ ,  $\epsilon_{\text{t-an}}$ ,  $\epsilon_{\text{iacr}}$  and  $\epsilon_{\text{rcca}}$ , resp., such that

$$\epsilon \leq 2 \epsilon_{\text{m-ind}} + (k+1) \epsilon_{\text{t-an}} + (2\ell+1) \epsilon_{\text{iacr}} + \epsilon_{\text{rcca}}.$$

The proof proceeds via an hybrid argument. We first recall game  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0}^{\mathtt{c-tr}}$ .

Experiment 
$$\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0}^{\mathtt{c-tr}}(\lambda)$$
:  
 $par \leftarrow \mathsf{ParamGen}(1^{\lambda}); \ (sk_{\mathcal{B}}, pk_{\mathcal{B}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{BKeyGen}(par)$ 

{49}------------------------------------------------

```
\mathcal{DCL}' := \emptyset; \ ctr \leftarrow 0
i_0 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist},\mathtt{BDepo'},\mathtt{Spy}}(par,pk_{\mathcal{B}},sk_{\mathcal{W}},sk_{\mathcal{D}})
Run Rcv(i_0) with \mathcal{A}
Let c_0 be the coin received
x_0 \leftarrow \mathsf{CheckDS}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, \emptyset, \mathcal{CL}, c_0)
If x_0 = \bot then ctr \leftarrow ctr + 1
\mathcal{DCL}' \leftarrow \mathsf{CheckDS}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, \emptyset, \emptyset, c_0)
i_1 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\texttt{URegist}, \texttt{BDepo}', \texttt{Spy}}
Run Rcv(i_1) with \mathcal{A}
Let c_1 be the coin received
x_1 \leftarrow \mathsf{CheckDS}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, \emptyset, \mathcal{CL}, c_1)
If x_1 = \bot then ctr \leftarrow ctr + 1
If comp(c_0, c_1) \neq 1 then return 0
x_2 \leftarrow \mathsf{CheckDS}(\mathit{sk}_{\mathcal{CK}}, \emptyset, \mathcal{DCL}', c_1)
If x_2 \neq \bot then \mathcal{DCL}' \leftarrow x_2
(\vec{i}^{(0)}, \dot{\vec{i}}^{(1)}) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist},\mathtt{BDepo}',\mathtt{Spy}}
Let k := |\vec{i}^{(0)}|; If k \neq |\vec{i}^{(1)}| then return 0
If k \neq 0 then run S\&R(1, (\vec{i}^{(0)})_1)
For j = 2, ..., k:
           Run S&R(j+1,(\vec{i}^{(0)})_j)
Run Spd(k+2) with \mathcal{A}
b^* \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{BDepo'}}; return b^*
                                                     // instead of CheckDS*, BDepo'
                                                uses CheckDS'(\cdot, \cdot, \cdot, \cdot, \mathcal{DCL}') defined as follows:
                            CheckDS'(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, \mathcal{UL}, \mathcal{DCL}, c, \mathcal{DCL}'):
                                        x \leftarrow \mathsf{CheckDS}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, \emptyset, \mathcal{DCL}', c)
                                        If x = \bot:
                                                    ctr \leftarrow ctr + 1
                                                   If ctr > 1 then return 0
                                        Return CheckDS(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, \emptyset, \mathcal{DCL}, c)
```

Note that we are only interested in detecting double spending, and not tracing the cheater (because CheckDS always run on an empty user list, which in our instantiation implies that it will never accuse someone and will output  $\bot$  when it detects a double-spending). We can therefore simplify CheckDS as follows (and the distribution of the output of the experiment will be unchanged):

```
CheckDS<sub>simple</sub>(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, \mathcal{UL}, \mathcal{DCL}, c):

sn \leftarrow \mathsf{E}'.\mathsf{Dec}(dk_{\mathrm{init}}, \tilde{c}_{sn}^{0})

If sn \in \mathcal{DCL} then return \bot

Else \mathcal{DCL} := \mathcal{DCL} \cup \{sn\}; return \mathcal{DCL}
```

Let  $\mathsf{CheckDS'_{simple}}$  and  $\mathsf{BDepo'_{simple}}$  be similar variants of  $\mathsf{CheckDS'}$  and  $\mathsf{BDepo'}$ , respectively, that use  $\mathsf{CheckDS_{simple}}$  instead of  $\mathsf{CheckDS}$ . The beginning of the proof will be very similar to the one of coin-anonymity.

{50}------------------------------------------------

Note that we choose to only keep the *initial* serial numbers in  $\mathcal{DCL}$ , since in this game we only check if there is double-spending or not (in particular, we do not send any proof of culpability). Thus only the first serial-number component of a coin matters, and it will not change in the following game.

<span id="page-50-0"></span>Using the same arguments as in Sect. A.3, we get the following.

**Proposition 29.** Expt<sup>c-tr</sup><sub>A,0</sub>( $\lambda$ ) and Expt<sup>c-tr</sup><sub>A,0,ZK</sub>( $\lambda$ ) are ( $\epsilon_{\text{m-ind}}+t\epsilon_{\text{t-an}}$ ) statistically close.

```
Experiment \mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{ZK}}^{\mathtt{c-tr}}(\lambda):
                Gr \leftarrow \mathsf{GrGen}(1^{\lambda})
                par_{\mathsf{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)
                par_{\mathsf{S}} \leftarrow \mathsf{S.Setup}(Gr)
                par_{\mathsf{S}'} \leftarrow \mathsf{S}'.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)
                (\mathit{ck}, \mathit{td}) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmSetup}(\mathit{Gr})
               par \leftarrow \boxed{(1^{\lambda}, par_{S}, par_{S'}, par_{T}, ck)}
               (pk_{\mathcal{B}}, s\overline{k_{\mathcal{B}}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{BKeyGen}
              \mathcal{DCL}' := \emptyset; \ ctr \leftarrow 0
              i_0 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist},\mathtt{BDepo'_{simple}},\mathtt{Spy}}(par,pk_{\mathcal{B}},sk_{\mathcal{W}},sk_{\mathcal{D}})
              Run Rcv_{ZK}(i_0) with A; let c_0 be the received coin
               x_0 \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{CheckDS}}_{\mathrm{simple}}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, \emptyset, \mathcal{CL}, c_0)
              If x_0 = \bot then ctr \leftarrow ctr + 1
              \mathcal{DCL'} \leftarrow \mathsf{CheckDS}_{\mathrm{simple}}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, \emptyset, \emptyset, c_0)i_1 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist}, \mathtt{BDepo'_{simple}}, \mathtt{Spy}}
              Run |\operatorname{Rcv}_{\operatorname{ZK}}|(i_1) with \mathcal{A}; let c_1 be the received coin
              x_1 \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{CheckDS}}_{\mathrm{simple}}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, \emptyset, \mathcal{CL}, c_1)
              If x_1 = \bot then ctr \leftarrow ctr + 1
               If comp(c_0, c_1) \neq 1 then return 0
              x_2 \leftarrow \mathsf{CheckDS}_{\mathsf{simple}}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, \emptyset, \mathcal{DCL}', c_1)
              If x_2 \neq \bot then \mathcal{DCL}' \leftarrow x_2
               (\vec{i}^{(0)}, \vec{i}^{(1)}) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist}, \mathtt{BDepo}'_{\mathrm{simple}}, \mathtt{Spy}}
              Let k be the size of \vec{i}^{(0)}
              If k is different of the size of \vec{i}^{(1)}: return 0
              If k \neq 0, then run \begin{bmatrix} \mathbb{S} \& \mathbb{R}_{\mathbb{Z} \mathbb{K}} \end{bmatrix} (1, (i^{\frac{1}{k}})_1)
               Then repeat the following for j = 3, ..., (k+1):
             \operatorname{Run} \left[ \operatorname{S\&R}_{\operatorname{ZK}} (j, (\overline{i}^{(1)})_{j-1}) \right]
\operatorname{Run} \left[ \operatorname{Spd}_{\operatorname{ZK}} (k+1) \text{ with } \mathcal{A} \right]
b^* \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\operatorname{BDepo'}_{\operatorname{simple}}} ; \operatorname{return} b^*
                                                                                              // BDepo_{\rm simple}' uses CheckDS_{\rm simple}'
```

Now we can leverage zero-knowledge and randomizability to partially "remelt (all the commits and proofs in)  $c_0$ . The strategy is the following: Using Extract,

{51}------------------------------------------------

defined below, we "break"  $c_0$  and  $c_1$  to extract all the relevant information (serial numbers, tags and nonce). Using Remelt we remelt both coins, after switching the following content:

- In  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{iacr}}^{c-tr}$ , we switch all the tags, and serial numbers (except the first serial number).
- In  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{rcca1}}^{\mathtt{c-tr}}$ , we switch the first serial numbers of both coins.
- In  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{final}}^{\mathtt{c-tr}}$ , we switch the nonces.

Thus we define the two followings procedures:

```
\begin{split} & \text{Extract}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}},c) \colon \\ & \text{Parse } c \text{ as:} \\ & \left(c^0, \left(c^k = (c_{pk}^k, c_{cert}^k, \pi_{cert}^k, c_{sn}^k, \pi_{sn}^k, c_{tag}^k, \pi_{tag}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{tag}^k, \tilde{\pi}_{sn}^k, \tilde{\pi}_{tag}^k)\right)_{k=1}^{\ell}, \\ & sn_0 = \mathsf{E}'.\mathsf{Dec}(dk_{\mathrm{init}}, \tilde{c}_{sn}^0) \\ & \text{Return } \left(sn_0, n, (\tilde{c}_{sn}^1, \dots, \tilde{c}_{sn}^\ell), (\tilde{c}_{tag}^1, \dots, \tilde{c}_{tag}^\ell)\right) \\ & \text{Remelt}(td, \tilde{c}_{sn}, n, (\tilde{c}_{sn}^1, \dots, \tilde{c}_{sn}^\ell), (\tilde{c}_{tag}^1, \dots, \tilde{c}_{tag}^\ell)) \\ & \rho_{sn}^0, \rho_{\mathrm{cert}}^0, \rho_{pk}^0, \rho_{m}^0, \rho_{\sigma}^0 \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{R} \\ & c_{sn}, c_{\mathrm{cert}}, c_{pk}, c_{M}, c_{\sigma} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{sn}^0, \rho_{\mathrm{cert}}^0, \rho_{pk}^0, \rho_{m}^0, \rho_{\sigma}^0) \\ & \pi_{cert} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmPrv}(td, \mathsf{S}'.\mathsf{Verify}(vk', \cdot, \cdot) = 1, \rho_{pk}^0, \rho_{\sigma}^0) \\ & \pi_{\sigma} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmPrv}(td, \mathsf{S.Verify}(vk, \cdot, \cdot) = 1, \rho_{m}^0, \rho_{\sigma}^0) \\ & \pi_{sn} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmPrv}_{sn, \mathrm{init}}(td, \rho_{pk}^0, \rho_{sn}^0, \rho_{m}^0) \\ & \tilde{\pi}_{sn} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmPrv}_{enc}(td, ek', \rho_{sn}^0, \tilde{c}_{sn}^0) \\ & c^0 \leftarrow (c_{pk}, c_{cert}, \pi_{cert}, c_{sn}, \pi_{sn}, c_M, c_{\sigma}, \pi_{\sigma}, \tilde{c}_{sn}, \tilde{\pi}_{sn}) \\ & \mathsf{For } k \in \{1, \dots, \ell\} \colon \\ & \rho_{sn}^k, \rho_{cert}^k, \rho_{pk}^k, \rho_{tag}^k, \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{R} \\ & c_{sn}^k, c_{tag}^k, c_{pk}^k, c_{n}^k, c_{\sigma}^k \leftarrow \mathsf{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{sn}^k, \rho_{tag}^k, \rho_{pk}^k, \rho_{m}^k, \rho_{\sigma}^k) \\ & \pi_{sn}^k \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmPrv}_{sn}(td, s'.\mathsf{Verify}(vk', \cdot, \cdot) = 1, \rho_{pk}^k, \rho_{cert}^k) \\ & \pi_{sn}^k \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmPrv}_{sn}(td, \rho_{pk}^k, \rho_{sn}^k) \\ & \tilde{\pi}_{sn}^k \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmPrv}_{sn}(td, ek, \rho_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k) \\ & \tilde{\pi}_{tag}^k \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmPrv}_{enc}(td, ek, \rho_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^k, \tilde{c}_{sn}^
```

<span id="page-51-0"></span>By the zero-knowledge property of C, the outputs of  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{ZK}}^{\mathtt{c-tr}}(\lambda)$  and  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{remelt}}^{\mathtt{c-tr}}(\lambda)$  will follow perfectly the same distribution:

**Proposition 30.** Expt<sup>c-tr</sup><sub> $\mathcal{A},0,\text{remelt}$ </sub>( $\lambda$ ) and Expt<sup>c-tr</sup><sub> $\mathcal{A},0,\text{ZK}$ </sub>( $\lambda$ ) are equally distributed.

```
Experiment \mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{remelt}}^{\mathtt{c-tr}}(\lambda):
Gr \leftarrow \mathsf{GrGen}(1^{\lambda})
par_{\mathsf{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr) \; ; \; par_{\mathsf{S}} \leftarrow \mathsf{S}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr) \; ; \; par_{\mathsf{S}'} \leftarrow \mathsf{S}'.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)
(ck,td) \leftarrow \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{SmSetup}(Gr)
```

{52}------------------------------------------------

```
par \leftarrow (1^{\lambda}, par_{S}, par_{S'}, par_{T}, ck)
(pk_{\mathcal{B}}, sk_{\mathcal{B}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{BKeyGen}()
\mathcal{DCL}' := \emptyset; \ ctr \leftarrow 0
i_0 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist},\mathtt{BDepo}'_{\mathrm{simple}},\mathtt{Spy}}(par,pk_{\mathcal{B}},sk_{\mathcal{W}},sk_{\mathcal{D}})

 \mathcal{DCL}' := \overline{\{sn_0, sn_1\}}

 \mathcal{CL}[1].c \leftarrow c_0'

Then repeat the following for j = 3, ..., (k + 1):
            Run S&R<sub>ZK</sub>(j, (\vec{i}^{(1)})_{j-1})
Run \operatorname{Spd}_{\operatorname{ZK}}(k+1) with \mathcal{A}
b^* \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\texttt{BDepo}'_{\text{simple}}}; return b^*
```

The serial numbers and tags are encrypted. We can change the ciphertexts encrypted with E in Extract; each switch will affect the distribution of the output of the overall experiment with probability at most  $\epsilon_{iacr}$ . We deduce the following:

<span id="page-52-0"></span>**Proposition 31.** Expt<sup>c-tr</sup><sub> $\mathcal{A},0,\text{remelt}$ </sub>( $\lambda$ ) and Expt<sup>c-tr</sup><sub> $\mathcal{A},0,\text{iacr}$ </sub>( $\lambda$ ) are  $2\ell$ -statistically close.

```
Experiment \mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{iacr}}^{\mathtt{c-tr}}(\lambda):
Gr \leftarrow \mathsf{GrGen}(1^{\lambda})
par_{\mathsf{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr) \; ; \; par_{\mathsf{S}} \leftarrow \mathsf{S}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr) \; ; \; par_{\mathsf{S}'} \leftarrow \mathsf{S'}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)
(ck,td) \leftarrow \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{SmSetup}(Gr)
par \leftarrow (1^{\lambda},par_{\mathsf{S}},par_{\mathsf{S'}},par_{\mathsf{T}},ck)
(pk_{\mathcal{B}},sk_{\mathcal{B}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{BKeyGen}
\mathcal{DCL'} := \emptyset; \; ctr \leftarrow 0
i_0 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{URegist},\mathsf{BDepo'},\mathsf{Spy}}(par,pk_{\mathcal{B}},sk_{\mathcal{W}},sk_{\mathcal{D}})
```

{53}------------------------------------------------

```
x_0 \leftarrow \mathsf{CheckDS}_{\mathrm{simple}}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, \emptyset, \mathcal{CL}, c_0)
            If x_0 = \bot then ctr \leftarrow ctr + 1
            i_1 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist},\mathtt{BDepo}',\mathtt{Spy}}
            Run Rcv(i_1) with A; let c_1 be the received coin
            x_1 \leftarrow \mathsf{CheckDS}_{\mathsf{simple}}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, \emptyset, \mathcal{CL}, c_1)
            If x_1 = \bot then ctr \leftarrow ctr + 1
            If comp(c_0, c_1) \neq 1 abort the entire procedure
            sn_0, n^{(0)}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{sn,0}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{tag,0} \leftarrow \texttt{Extract}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, c_0)
            sn_1, n^{(1)}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{sn,1}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{tag,1} \leftarrow \texttt{Extract}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, c_1)
            \nu \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{R}
            \tilde{c}_{sn} \leftarrow \mathsf{E}'.\mathsf{Enc}(ek',sn_0,\nu)
            c_0' \leftarrow \mathtt{Remelt}(td, \tilde{c}_{sn}, n^{(0)}, \boxed{\vec{c}_{sn,1}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{tag,1}})
            \mathcal{DCL}' := \{sn_0, sn_1\}
            (\vec{i}^{(0)}, \vec{i}^{(1)}) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist},\mathtt{BDepo}'_{\mathrm{simple}},\mathtt{Spy}}
            Let k be the size of \vec{i}^{(0)}
            If k is different of the size of \vec{i}^{(1)} abort
            \mathcal{CL}[1].c \leftarrow c_0'
            Run S&R<sub>ZK</sub>(1, (\vec{i}^{(1)})_1)
            Then repeat the following step for j = 3, ..., (k+1):
                         Run S&R<sub>ZK</sub>(j, (\vec{i}^{(1)})_{j-1})
            Run \operatorname{Spd}_{\operatorname{ZK}}(k+1) with \mathring{\mathcal{A}}
            b^* \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\text{BDepo'}_{\text{simple}}}; return b^*
For the next step, we will rely on RCCA-security of E'.
Experiment \mathbf{Expt}^{\mathtt{c-tr}}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{rcca}}(Gr,ek'):
            par_{\mathsf{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr) \; ; \; par_{\mathsf{S}} \leftarrow \mathsf{S}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr) \; ; \; par_{\mathsf{S}'} \leftarrow \mathsf{S}'.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)
            (ck, td) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmSetup}(Gr)
             par \leftarrow (1^{\lambda}, par_{S}, par_{S'}, par_{T}, ck)
                (vk, sk) \leftarrow \mathsf{S.KeyGen}
                (vk', sk') \leftarrow \mathsf{S.KeyGen}
                (ek, dk) \leftarrow \mathsf{E.KeyGen}
              \mathit{pk}_{\mathcal{B}} := (\mathit{ek}', \mathit{ek}, \mathit{vk}, \mathit{vk}')
              sk_{\mathcal{W}} := (sk, sk')
             \mathcal{DCL}' := \emptyset; \ ctr \leftarrow 0
              (Use the \mathsf{Dec}\ \mathrm{oracle}\ \mathrm{call}\ \mathrm{in}\ \mathrm{all}\ \mathrm{the}\ \mathsf{BDepo}'_{\mathrm{simple}}\ \mathrm{call}\ \mathrm{from}\ \mathcal{A};)
            i_0 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\text{URegist}, \text{BDepo'}, \text{Spy}}(par, pk_{\mathcal{B}}, sk_{\mathcal{W}}, sk_{\mathcal{D}})
            Run Rcv(i_0) with A; et c_0 be the received coin
            x_0 \leftarrow \mathsf{CheckDS}_{\mathsf{simple}}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, \emptyset, \mathcal{CL}, c_0)
            If x_0 = \bot then ctr \leftarrow ctr + 1
            i_1 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist},\mathtt{BDepo'},\mathtt{Spy}}
```

Run  $Rcv(i_0)$  with A; let  $c_0$  be the received coin

{54}------------------------------------------------

```
Run Rcv(i_1) with A; let c_1 be the received coin
x_1 \leftarrow \mathsf{CheckDS}_{\mathrm{simple}}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, \emptyset, \mathcal{CL}, c_1)
If x_1 = \bot then ctr \leftarrow ctr + 1
If comp(c_0, c_1) \neq 1 abort the entire procedure
sn_0, n^{(0)}, \vec{sn}_0, \vec{tag}_0 \leftarrow \texttt{Extract}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, c_0)
sn_1, n^{(1)}, \vec{sn}_1, \vec{tag}_1 \leftarrow \texttt{Extract}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, c_1)
\mathcal{DCL}' := \{sn_0, sn_1\}
(\vec{i}^{(0)},\vec{i}^{(1)}) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist},\mathtt{BDepo}'_{\mathrm{simple}},\mathtt{Spy}}
Let k be the size of \vec{i}^{(0)}
If k is different of the size of \vec{i}^{(1)} abort
 Send sn_0, sn_1 as challenge for the rcca-security game and receive \tilde{c}
 c_0' \leftarrow \mathtt{Remelt}(td, \tilde{c}, n^{(0)}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{sn,1}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{tag,1})
 (insert the challenge \tilde{c} in this step as \tilde{c}_{sn}^0)
\mathcal{CL}[1].c \leftarrow c_0'
Run S&R<sub>ZK</sub>(1, (\vec{i}^{(1)})_1)
Then repeat the following step for j = 3, \ldots, (k+1):
          Run S&R<sub>ZK</sub>(j, (\vec{i}^{(1)})_{j-1})
Run \operatorname{Spd}_{\operatorname{ZK}}(k+1) with \mathcal A
b^* \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\texttt{BDepo}'_{\text{rcca}}} \text{ ; return } b^*
   \mathsf{CheckDS}'_{\mathsf{rcca}}(\mathit{sk}_{\mathcal{CK}}, \mathcal{UL}, \mathcal{DCL}, c,) \colon
             t \leftarrow \mathsf{E.GDec}(dk_{\mathrm{init}}, \tilde{c}_{sn}^0)
             If t = \text{"replay"} and ctr > 0 then abort the entire procedure
              Else if t = "replay" then ctr \leftarrow ctr + 1
              Else if t \in \mathcal{DCL} then return \perp
             Else add sn to \mathcal{DCL}, and return \mathcal{DCL}
```

<span id="page-54-0"></span>If the challenger of the RCCA security game encrypts  $sn_0$ , the resulting experiment will be  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{iacr}}^{\mathtt{c-tr}}(\lambda)$ ; otherwise it will be  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{rcca1}}^{\mathtt{c-tr}}(\lambda)$ . We thus deduce:

**Proposition 32.** Expt<sup>c-tr</sup><sub> $\mathcal{A},0,\text{iacr}$ </sub>( $\lambda$ ) and Expt<sup>c-tr</sup><sub> $\mathcal{A},0,\text{rcca1}$ </sub>( $\lambda$ ) are  $\epsilon_{\text{rcca}}$ -statistically close.

```
Experiment \mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{rcca1}}^{\mathtt{c-tr}}(\lambda):

Gr \leftarrow \mathsf{GrGen}(1^{\lambda})

par_{\mathsf{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr) \; ; \; par_{\mathsf{S}} \leftarrow \mathsf{S}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr) \; ; \; par_{\mathsf{S}'} \leftarrow \mathsf{S}'.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)

(ck,td) \leftarrow \mathsf{C}.\mathsf{SmSetup}(Gr)

par \leftarrow (1^{\lambda},par_{\mathsf{S}},par_{\mathsf{S}'},par_{\mathsf{T}},ck)

(pk_{\mathcal{B}},sk_{\mathcal{B}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{BKeyGen}

\mathcal{DCL}' := \emptyset; \; ctr \leftarrow 0

i_0 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{URegist},\mathsf{BDepo'},\mathsf{Spy}}(par,pk_{\mathcal{B}},sk_{\mathcal{W}},sk_{\mathcal{D}})

\mathsf{Run} \; \mathsf{Rcv}(i_0) \; \mathsf{with} \; \mathcal{A} \; ; \; \mathsf{let} \; c_0 \; \mathsf{be} \; \mathsf{the} \; \mathsf{received} \; \mathsf{coin}

x_0 \leftarrow \mathsf{CheckDS}_{\mathsf{simple}}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}},\emptyset,\mathcal{CL},c_0)

\mathsf{If} \; x_0 = \bot \; \mathsf{then} \; ctr \leftarrow ctr + 1

i_1 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{URegist},\mathsf{BDepo'},\mathsf{Spy}}
```

{55}------------------------------------------------

```
x_1 \leftarrow \mathsf{CheckDS}_{\mathrm{simple}}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, \emptyset, \mathcal{CL}, c_1)
             If x_1 = \bot then ctr \leftarrow ctr + 1
              If comp(c_0, c_1) \neq 1 abort the entire procedure
              sn_0, n^{(0)}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{sn,0}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{tag,0} \leftarrow \texttt{Extract}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, c_0)
              sn_1, n^{(1)}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{sn,1}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{tag,1} \leftarrow \texttt{Extract}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, c_1)
              \nu \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{R}
              \tilde{c}_{sn} \leftarrow \mathsf{E}'.\mathsf{Enc}(ek', \lceil sn_1 \rceil, \nu)
              c_0' \leftarrow \mathtt{Remelt}(td, \overleftarrow{\tilde{c}_{sn}, n}^{(0)}, \overrightarrow{\tilde{c}}_{sn,1}, \overrightarrow{\tilde{c}}_{tag,1})
              \mathcal{DCL}' := \{sn_0, sn_1\}
              (\vec{i}^{(0)}, \vec{i}^{(1)}) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist}, \mathtt{BDepo}'_{\mathrm{simple}}, \mathtt{Spy}}
             Let k be the size of \vec{i}^{(0)}
             If k is different of the size of \vec{i}^{(1)}: return 0
             \mathcal{CL}[1].c \leftarrow c_0'
             Run S&R<sub>ZK</sub>(1, (\vec{i}^{(1)})_1)
              Then repeat the following step for j = 3, ..., (k + 1):
                            Run S&R<sub>ZK</sub>(j, (\vec{i}^{(1)})_{j-1})
              Run \operatorname{Spd}_{\operatorname{ZK}}(k+1) with \mathcal A
              b^* \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\texttt{BDepo}'_{\text{simple}}}; return b^*
        We define:
S\&R_{ZK,tag}(j,i,n^{(0)},sk^{(0)}):
              c := \mathcal{CL}[j].c
             u := \mathcal{CL}[j].owner
             n' \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{N} ; \rho'_{sn}, \rho'_{cert}, \rho'_{pk}, \rho'_{sn-pf}, \nu'_{sn} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{R}; Compute:
                            (sn', sn\text{-}pf') \leftarrow \mathsf{T.SGen}(par_{\mathsf{T}}, \mathcal{UL}[i].sk, n')
                            c_{cert}', c_{pk}', c_{sn}', c_{sn\text{-}pf}' \leftarrow \mathsf{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{cert}', \rho_{pk}', \rho_{sn}', \rho_{sn\text{-}pf}')
                            \tilde{c}'_{sn} \leftarrow \mathsf{E.Enc}(ek, sn', \nu'_{sn})
                            \pi'_{cert} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmPrv} \big( td, \mathsf{S.Verify}(vk', \cdot, \cdot) = 1, \rho'_{vk}, \rho'_{pk}, \rho'_{cert} \big)
                            \pi'_{sn} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmPrv}_{sn}(td, pk'_{tag}, sn', sn\text{-}pf, \rho'_{pk}, \rho'_{sn}, \rho'_{sn\text{-}pf})
                            \tilde{\pi}'_{\mathrm{sn}} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmPrv}_{\mathrm{enc}}(td, ek, \rho'_{\mathrm{sn}}, \tilde{c}'_{\mathrm{sn}})
              Decompose c as
              (c^0, (c^j = (c^j_{pk}, c^j_{cert}, \pi^j_{cert}, c^j_{sn}, \pi^j_{sn}, c^j_{tag}, \pi^j_{tag}, \tilde{c}^j_{sn}, \tilde{c}^j_{tag}, \tilde{\pi}^j_{sn}, \tilde{\pi}^j_{tag}))^i_{j=1},
                            n, \mathrm{sn}, \rho_{\mathrm{sn}}, \rho_{\mathrm{pk}}
              \rho_{tag}, \nu_{tag}, \rho_{t-pf} \xleftarrow{\$} \mathcal{R}
               (tag, t\text{-}pf) \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{TGen}(par_{\mathsf{T}}, \mathcal{UL}[u].sk, n, sn')
                (tag^{(0)}, P_{tag}^{(0)}) \leftarrow \mathsf{T.TGen}(par_\mathsf{T}, sk^{(0)}, n^{(0)}, sn')
              \overline{c_{tag} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.ZCm}(ck, \rho_{tag})}
              \tilde{c}_{tag} \leftarrow \left| \text{ E.Enc}(ek, tag^{(0)}, \nu_{tag}) \right|
              \pi_{tag} \leftarrow \overline{\mathsf{C.SmPrv}_{tag}(td, pk_{tag}, sn, sn', tag, t\text{-}pf, \rho_{pk}, \rho_{sn}, \rho'_{sn}, \rho_{tag}, \rho_{t\text{-}pf})}
              \tilde{\pi}_{tag} \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmPrv}_{enc}(td, ek, \rho_{tag}, \tilde{c}_{tag})
```

Run  $Rcv(i_1)$  with A; let  $c_1$  be the received coin

{56}------------------------------------------------

<span id="page-56-0"></span>Compute 
$$\mathsf{VER}_{\mathsf{init}}(c^0) \wedge \bigwedge_{j=1}^i \mathsf{VER}_{\mathsf{std}}(c^{j-1}, c^j) \wedge \mathsf{T.TVfy}(ck, c^i_{pk}, c'_{sn}, c_{tag}, \pi_{tag}) \wedge \mathsf{C.Verify}_{\mathsf{enc}}(ck, ek, c_{tag}, \tilde{c}_{tag}, \tilde{\pi}_{tag})$$
 Pick uniformly at random a vector of randomness  $\vec{\rho''}$   $c'' \leftarrow \mathsf{Rand}((c^0, (c^j)^i_{j=1}, c'_{pk}, c'_{\mathsf{cert}}, \pi'_{\mathsf{cert}}, c'_{sn}, \pi'_{sn}, c_{tag}, \pi_{tag}, \tilde{c}'_{sn}, \tilde{\pi}'_{sn}, \tilde{c}'_{tag}, \tilde{\pi}'_{tag}), \vec{\rho''})$   $c_{new} := (c'', n', \mathsf{sn'}, \rho'_{\mathsf{sn}} + (\vec{\rho''})_{\mathsf{sn'}}, \rho'_{pk} + (\vec{\rho''})_{pk'})$   $\mathcal{CL}[|\mathcal{CL}| + 1] := (i, c_{new}, 0, j)$ 

We substituted one ciphertext for another in the previous algorithm and get:

Proposition 33.  $Expt_{\mathcal{A},0,rcca1}^{c-tr}$  and  $Expt_{\mathcal{A},0,final}^{c-tr}$  are  $\epsilon_{iacr}$  statistically close.

```
Experiment \mathbf{Expt}^{\mathtt{c-tr}}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{final}}(\lambda):
            Gr \leftarrow \mathsf{GrGen}(1^{\lambda})
            par_{\mathsf{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{T}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr) \; ; \; par_{\mathsf{S}} \leftarrow \mathsf{S}.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr) \; ; \; par_{\mathsf{S}'} \leftarrow \mathsf{S}'.\mathsf{Setup}(Gr)
            (ck, td) \leftarrow \mathsf{C.SmSetup}(Gr)
            par \leftarrow (1^{\lambda}, par_{S}, par_{S'}, par_{T}, ck)
             (pk_{\mathcal{B}}, sk_{\mathcal{B}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{BKeyGen}
             \mathcal{DCL}' := \emptyset; \ ctr \leftarrow 0
            i_0 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist},\mathtt{BDepo'},\mathtt{Spy}}(par,pk_{\mathcal{B}},sk_{\mathcal{W}},sk_{\mathcal{D}})
            Run Rcv(i_0) with \mathcal{A}; let c_0 be the received coin
            i_1 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\texttt{URegist}, \texttt{BDepo}', \texttt{Spy}}
            Run Rcv(i_1) with \mathcal{A}; let c_1 be the received coin
            If comp(c_0, c_1) \neq 1 abort the entire procedure
            sn_0, n^{(0)}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{sn,0}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{tag,0} \leftarrow \texttt{Extract}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, c_0)
            sn_1, n^{(1)}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{sn,1}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{tag,1} \leftarrow \texttt{Extract}(sk_{\mathcal{CK}}, c_1)
            \nu \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathcal{R}
            \tilde{c}_{sn} \leftarrow \mathsf{E}'.\mathsf{Enc}(ek',sn_1,\nu)
             c_0' \leftarrow \mathtt{Remelt}(td, \tilde{c}_{sn}, n^{(0)}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{sn,1}, \vec{\tilde{c}}_{tag,1})
            \mathcal{DCL}' := \{sn_0, sn_1\}
             (\vec{i}^{(0)}, \vec{i}^{(1)}) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{URegist}, \mathtt{BDepo}'_{\mathrm{simple}}, \mathtt{Spy}}
            Let k be the size of \vec{i}^{(0)}
            If k is different of the size of \vec{i}^{(1)}: return 0
            \mathcal{CL}[1].c \leftarrow c_0'
            Run | S\&R_{ZK,tag}(1,(\vec{i}^{(1)})_1,n^{(1)},sk) |
            Then repeat the following step for j = 3, ..., (k+1):
                          Run S&R<sub>ZK</sub>(j, (\vec{i}^{(1)})_{j-1})
            Run \operatorname{Spd}_{\operatorname{ZK}}(k+1) with \widehat{\mathcal{A}}
            b^* \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathtt{BDepo}'_{\mathrm{simple}}}; return b^*
```

We note that

$$\mathbf{Expt}^{\mathtt{c-tr}}_{\mathcal{A},0,\mathrm{final}}(\lambda) = \mathbf{Expt}^{\mathtt{c-tr}}_{\mathcal{A},1,\mathrm{ZK}}(\lambda).$$

It is  $\epsilon_{\text{m-ind}}$ -close to  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},1}^{\mathbf{c-tr}}(\lambda)$ . By combining this last remark with Propositions 29, 30, 31, 32 and 33, this proves the theorem.

{57}------------------------------------------------

# **B** Instantiation

### <span id="page-57-0"></span>B.1 Instantiation and proofs of the double spending tag scheme

We will reuse the scheme introduced in [BCFK15], which we recall here.

```
T.Setup (Gr):
       - Parse Gr as (p, \mathbb{G}, \hat{\mathbb{G}}, \mathbb{G}_T, e, g_1, \hat{g})
       -g_2, h_1, h_2 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{G}
       - Return (g_1 = g, g_2, h_1, h_2)
    We define \mathcal{M} = \{(g_1^m, \hat{g}^m) \in \mathbb{G} \times \hat{\mathbb{G}}\}_{m \in \mathbb{Z}_n}
T.KeyGen(par_T):
       -sk \stackrel{*}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p
       - Return (sk_T := sk, pk_T := \hat{g}^{sk})
T.SGen<sub>init</sub> (par_{\mathsf{T}}, sk_{\mathsf{T}}, n):
- M \leftarrow g_1^n ; N \leftarrow g_2^{n+sk_{\mathsf{T}}}
       -M_{sn}^{(1)} = (g_1^n, \hat{g}^n) ; M_{sn}^{(2)} = (g_1^{sk_\mathsf{T}}, \hat{g}^{sk_\mathsf{T}})
       - Return (sn = (M, N), M_{sn} = (M_{sn}^{(1)}, M_{sn}^{(2)}))
T.SGen (par_{\mathsf{T}}, sk_{\mathsf{T}}, n):
      - \stackrel{\frown}{M} \leftarrow g_1^n ; \stackrel{\frown}{N} \leftarrow g_2^{n+sk_{\mathsf{T}}} \\ - sn\text{-}pf = \hat{g}^n
       - Return (sn = (M, N), sn-pf)
T.TGen (par_T, sk, n, sn = (M, N)):
       - M_0 \leftarrow g_1^n 
- tag := (M^{sk}h_1^n, N^{sk}h_2^n)
       -t-pf \leftarrow \hat{q}^n
       - Return (tag := (A, B), t\text{-}pf).
T.Detect (sn, sn', tag, tag', \mathcal{L}):
       – Parse sn as (M,N); parse sn' as (M',N')
       - Parse tag as (A, B); parse tag' as (A', B')
       -A'' := \frac{A}{A'} ; B'' := \frac{B}{B'}
       -M'' := \frac{M}{M'} ; N'' := \frac{N}{N'}
       - If A'' = 0_{G_1} then:
                       A'' := B'' ; M'' := N''
       - Search pk_T in \mathcal{L} such that e(A'', \hat{g}) = e(M'', pk)
       - Return (pk_{\mathsf{T}}, (A'', M''))
T.VfyGuilt (pk, \pi):
       - Parse \pi as (A, N);
       - Return (e(A, \hat{g}) = e(N, pk) \land A \neq 0_{G_1}).
\mathsf{T.SVfy}_{\mathrm{init}}(par_{\mathsf{T}},pk_{\mathsf{T}},sn,M_{sn}):
       - Parse sn as (M, N)
       - Parse M_{sn} as ((M_1, \hat{M}_1), (M_2, \hat{M}_2))
       - Return (e(M, \hat{g})e(g_1^{-1}, \hat{M}_1) = 1_{G_T} \wedge e(M, \hat{g})e(g_2^{-1}, \hat{M}_2)e(g_2^{-1}, pk_T) =
           1_{G_T} \wedge \hat{M}_2 = pk_\mathsf{T} \wedge e(M_1, \hat{g}) = e(g_1, \hat{M}_1) \wedge e(M_2, \hat{g}) = e(g_1, \hat{M}_2)
```

{58}------------------------------------------------

```
\begin{split} \mathsf{T.SVfy}(par_{\mathsf{T}},pk_{\mathsf{T}},sn,sn\text{-}pf) \colon & - \; \mathsf{Parse} \; sn \; \mathsf{as} \; (M,N) \\ & - \; \mathsf{Return} \; \left( e(M,\hat{g})e(g_1^{-1},sn\text{-}pf) = 1_{G_T} \wedge \\ & \quad e(N,\hat{g})e(g_2^{-1},sn\text{-}pf)e(g_2^{-1},pk_{\mathsf{T}}) = 1_{G_T} \right) \\ \mathsf{T.TVfy}(par_{\mathsf{T}},pk,sn,sn',tag,t\text{-}pf) \colon & - \; \mathsf{Parse} \; sn \; \mathsf{as} \; (M,N) \\ & - \; \mathsf{Parse} \; sn \; \mathsf{as} \; (M,N) \\ & - \; \mathsf{Parse} \; tag \; \mathsf{as} \; (A,B) \\ & - \; \mathsf{Parse} \; sn' \; \mathsf{as} \; (M',N') \\ & - \; \mathsf{Return} \; \left( e(M,\hat{g})e(g_1^{-1},t\text{-}pf) = 1_{G_T} \wedge \\ & \quad e(A,\hat{g}^{-1})e(M',pk)e(h_1,t\text{-}pf) = 1_{G_T} \wedge \\ & \quad e(B,\hat{g}^{-1})e(N',pk)e(h_2,t\text{-}pf) = 1_{G_T} \right) \end{split}
```

#### **Proofs**

**Theorem 34.** This above scheme is extractable, bootable, SN-verifiable, tagverifiable and  $\mathcal N$  injective.

These properties are all straightforward to show and we therefore omit the proof.

**Proposition 35.** The above scheme is SN-collision-resistant.

Let (pk, sn-pf) and (pk', sn-pf') such that for some sn:

$$\mathsf{T.SVfy}(par_\mathsf{T}, pk, sn, sn\text{-}pf) = \mathsf{T.SVfy}(par, pk', sn, sn\text{-}pf') = 1.$$

We parse sn as (M, N), and deduce the followings equations:

$$e(M, \hat{g}) = e(g_1, sn-pf) = e(g_1, sn-pf'),$$

from which we get sn-pf = sn-pf'. Then we can deduce

$$e(M, \hat{g})e(g_2^{-1}, \text{sn-pf})e(g_2^{-1}, pk) = 0_{G_T} = e(M, \hat{g})e(g_2^{-1}, \text{sn-pf})e(g_2^{-1}, pk')$$

and thus  $e(g_2^{-1},pk)=e(g_2^{-1},pk')$ , which finally yields pk=pk'. The reasoning is analogous for T.SVfy<sub>init</sub>.

To prove the two other results, we will use the following lemma.

$$\begin{aligned} \mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},b}^{Tuple}(\lambda) \colon & & O_0' \colon \\ & ((\mathbb{G}, g_1, q), (\hat{\mathbb{G}}, \hat{g}, q), e) \leftarrow \mathsf{GrGen}(1^{\lambda}) \\ & g_2, h_1, h_2 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{G} \\ & b' \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{O_b'} \\ & \mathsf{Return} \ b = b' \end{aligned} \qquad \begin{aligned} & O_0' \colon \\ & n \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_q \\ & \mathsf{Return} \ (g_1^n, g_2^n, h_1^n, h_2^n) \\ & O_1' \colon \\ & n_1, n_2, n_3, n_4 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_q \\ & \mathsf{Return} \ (g_1^{n_1}, g_2^{n_2}, h_1^{n_3}, h_2^{n_4}) \end{aligned}$$

<span id="page-58-0"></span>**Lemma 36.** For any adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  against the game Tuple defined above with advantage  $\epsilon$ , there exists an adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  against DDH in  $\mathbb{G}$  with advantage  $\epsilon_{\mathrm{DDH}}$  such that  $\frac{\epsilon}{3K} \leq \epsilon_{\mathrm{DDH}}$ , with K the number of oracles calls to  $O_b'$ .

{59}------------------------------------------------

We define the following oracles:

$$O_{0.3}': \qquad \qquad O_{0.7}': \\ n, n_2 \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_q \qquad \qquad n, n_2, n_3 \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_q \\ \text{Return } (g_1^n, g_2^{n_2}, h_1^n, h_2^n) \qquad \qquad \text{Return } (g_1^n, g_2^{n_2}, h_1^{n_3}, h_2^n)$$

Viewing the tuples  $(g_2, g_1^n, g_2^n)$ ,  $(h_1, g_1^n, h_1^n)$  and  $(h_2, g_1^n, h_2^n)$  as DDH challenge tuples, we get taht the adversary cannot distinguish  $O'_0$  from  $O'_{0.3}$  nor  $O'_{0.3}$  from  $O'_{0.7}$ , or  $O'_{0.7}$  from  $O'_1$ , with probability more than  $\epsilon_{\text{DDH}}$  each respectively. (Note that we can compute all other elements, since we know the discrete logarithms of the elements which are not part of the respective DDH-tuple; and we can answer all other oracle calls honestly). This proves the lemma.

<span id="page-59-0"></span>Corollary 37. No adversary can break tag-anonymity with an advantage better than  $6K\epsilon_{DDH}$ , where K is the number of calls to  $O_1$ .

$$\begin{aligned} \mathbf{Expt}^{\mathsf{Perfect-tag-anonymity}}_{\mathcal{A},b}((\mathbb{G},g_1,q),(\hat{\mathbb{G}},\hat{g},q),e) \colon & D_1^{\mathsf{perfect}}(sk) \colon \\ par_{\mathsf{T}} \leftarrow ((\mathbb{G},g_1,q),(\hat{\mathbb{G}},\hat{g},q),e) & \mathsf{Return} \ (g_3,g_4,g_5,g_6) \leftarrow O_0' \\ (sk_0,sk_1) \leftarrow \mathcal{A} \ (par_{\mathsf{T}}) & \mathsf{Return} \ (g_3,g_1^{sk} \cdot g_4) & \mathsf{Q}_2^{\mathsf{perfect}}(sk_b), O_2^{\mathsf{perfect}}(sk_b,\cdot,\cdot) \ (par_{\mathsf{T}},sk_0,sk_1) & \mathsf{G}_2^{\mathsf{perfect}}(sk,sn',t) \colon \\ \mathsf{Return} \ (b=b^*) & \mathsf{G}_2^{\mathsf{perfect}} \ (sk,sn',t) \colon \\ \mathsf{If} \ t > k \ \mathsf{abort} \ \mathsf{entire} \ \mathsf{game} \ (g_5,g_6) \leftarrow T[t] \\ (N,M) \leftarrow sn' \\ \mathsf{Return} \ (Ng_5,Mg_6) & \mathsf{Return} \ (Ng_5,Mg_6) & \mathsf{Return} \ (Ng_5,Mg_6) & \mathsf{Return} \ (Ng_5,Mg_6) & \mathsf{Return} \ (Ng_5,Mg_6) & \mathsf{Return} \ Lemma 36 implies that the adversary cannot, except with probability  $3K\epsilon_{\text{DDH}}$ , distinguish Perfect-tag-anonymity from tag-anonymity: if we replace  $O_0'$  by  $O_1'$ , the game becomes exactly tag-anonymity. In the latter game, we can replace b by (1-b) without changing the distribution of the adversary's input.

**Theorem 38.** Let  $\mathcal{A}$  be an adversary that wins the exculpability game with probability  $\epsilon$  after K oracle calls to  $O_1$ , then there exist  $\mathcal{B}_1$  against DDH in  $\mathbb{G}$  with advantage  $\epsilon_{\mathrm{DDH}}$  and  $\mathcal{B}_2$  against DDH in  $\hat{\mathbb{G}}$  with advantage  $\hat{\epsilon}_{\mathrm{DDH}}$ , such that:

$$\epsilon \leq 3K\epsilon_{\rm DDH} + \hat{\epsilon}_{\rm DDH}$$
.

Using the same argument as in Corollary 37, we deduce, incurring a loss of  $3K\epsilon_{\text{DDH}}$ , that we can consider that oracle calls do not yield any information to the adversary. After receiving a triple  $(\hat{g}_1, \hat{g}_2, \hat{g}_3)$  in  $\hat{\mathbb{G}}$ , we send  $\hat{g}_1$  as the public key. When we receive (N, A) such that

$$e(N, pk) = e(A, \hat{g})$$

with  $A \neq 0_{\mathbb{G}_1}$ , this means that  $A = N^{\log_{g_1}(pk)}$  and we can check if  $e(N, \hat{g}_3) = e(A, \hat{g}_2)$  to decide whether we received a DDH triple or not.

{60}------------------------------------------------

**Efficiency** We summarize all the efficiency results as follows (where "m.s.w.u" means multiscalar with unknown):

| $ par_{T} $                                           | $3 \mathbb{G} $                                           |
|-------------------------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------|
| $ sk_{T} $                                            | $ \mathbb{Z}_p $                                          |
| $ pk_{T} $                                            | $ \hat{\mathbb{G}} $                                      |
| sn  =  tag                                            | $2 \mathbb{G} $                                           |
| sn-pf  =  t-pf                                        | Ĝ                                                         |
| $\pi$                                                 | $2 \mathbb{G} $                                           |
| Number of pairing equations in T.SVfy                 | 2 generic eq.                                             |
| Number of pairing equations in T.SVfy <sub>init</sub> | 4 generic, 1 m.s.w.u eq. in $\hat{\mathbb{G}}$            |
| Number of pairing equations in T.TVfy                 | 3 generic eq.                                             |
| $ \pi_{sn} $                                          | $8 \mathbb{G}  + 8 \hat{\mathbb{G}} $                     |
| $ \pi_{sn,\text{init}} $                              | $16 \mathbb{G}  + 16 \hat{\mathbb{G}}  + 2 \mathbb{Z}_p $ |
| $ \pi_{tag} $                                         | $12 \mathbb{G}  + 12 \hat{\mathbb{G}} $                   |
| $ \tilde{\pi}_{sn} $                                  | $8 \mathbb{G}  + 10 \hat{\mathbb{G}} $                    |
| $ \tilde{\pi}_{tag} $                                 | $12 \mathbb{G}  + 14 \hat{\mathbb{G}} $                   |

# <span id="page-60-0"></span>B.2 Instantiation of the encryption scheme E'

Construction overview. We roughly follow the framework proposed by Chase et al. [CKLM12]. The first part of the ciphertext is an encryption

$$\vec{C} = (c_0, c_1, \dots, c_{n+1}) = (f^{\theta}, g^{\theta}, \{h_i^{\theta} \cdot m_i\}_{i=1}^n)$$

of the message vector  $\vec{m} = (m_1, \dots, m_n) \in \mathbb{G}_n$ . As in [LPQ17], we use the same one-time linearly homomorphic structure-preserving signature scheme [LPJY13] LHSPS = (KeyGen, Sign. Verify), for which let

$$\vec{v}_1 = (f, g, 1, \dots, 1), \vec{v}_2 = (1, 1, 1, g, h_1, \dots, h_n),$$

the signing key of the LHSPS is composed of two linearly homomorphic signatures of  $\vec{v}_1$  and  $\vec{v}_2$ , that is,  $sk = (\sigma_{\vec{v}_1}, \sigma_{\vec{v}_2})$ . Using this signing key, anyone can generate the signature  $\sigma_{\vec{m}}$  of any message  $\vec{m} \in Span(\vec{v}_1, \vec{v}_2)$ .

The second part of the ciphertext is a zero-knowledge proof for the language

$$\mathcal{L}_{\vee} = \big\{ (\vec{C}, (b, \theta, \{m_i\}_{i=1}^n, \sigma_{\vec{v}})) \mid b \in \{0, 1\} \vee \mathsf{LHSPS.Verify}(vk_{\mathsf{LHSPS}}, \sigma_{\vec{v}}, \vec{v}) = 1 \big\}.$$

where  $\vec{v} = (c_0^b, c_1^b, g^{1-b}, c_1^{(1-b)}, c_2^{(1-b)}, \dots, c_{n+1}^{1-b})$ . Note that when b = 1,  $\vec{v} \in Span(\vec{v}_1, \vec{v}_2)$  means that  $\log_f(c_0) = \log_g(c_1)$ , then the ciphertext is a valid ciphertext. Also note that signatures on  $\vec{v}$  with b = 1 will only be generated in the security proof.

To enable re-randomization, we generate a signature  $\sigma_{\vec{w}}$  on the vector  $\vec{w} = (f^b, g^b, 1, g^{(1-b)\cdot\theta}, h_1^{(1-b)\cdot\theta}, \dots, h_n^{(1-b)\cdot\theta})$  and add a zero-knowledge proof of knowledge of the valid signature  $\sigma_{\vec{w}}$ . It is easy to see that with  $\sigma_{\vec{w}}$ , we can generate signatures for all re-randomization of the vector  $\vec{v}$ .

{61}------------------------------------------------

One-time linearly homomorphic structure-preserving signature. To construct the re-randomizable CCA encryption scheme, we need the one-time linearly homomorphic structure-preserving signature.

Definition 39 ((One-time) linearly homomorphic structure-preserving signature [LPJY13]). A one-time linearly homomorphic structure-preserving signature is tuple of 4 algorithms LHSPS = (Setup, Sign, SignDerive, Verify) with the following specifications:

- Setup (Gr, n) is a probabilistic algorithm taking the group parameter Gr and an integer n denoting the dimension of the message to be signed. It outputs the public verification key vk and the signature key sk.
- Sign  $(sk, \vec{m})$  is a deterministic algorithm that takes the signing key sk and the message  $\vec{m} \in \mathbb{G}^n$ , and outputs a signature  $\sigma$ .
- SignDerive  $(vk, \{(w_i, \sigma^{(i)})\}_{i=1}^{\ell})$  is a deterministic algorithm taking the verification key vk and  $\ell$  pairs  $(w_i\sigma^{(i)})$  where  $w_i \in \mathbb{Z}_p$  and  $\sigma^{(i)}$  is an LHSPS signature. It outputs a signature  $\sigma$  on the message  $\vec{m} = \prod_{i=1}^{\ell} \vec{m}_i^{w_i}$ .
- Verify  $(vk, \vec{m}, \sigma)$  is a deterministic algorithm taking the verification key vk, the message vector  $\vec{m}$  and a signature  $\sigma$ . It outputs 1 if the signature is valid, 0 otherwise.

**Definition 40 (One-time unforgeability).** A one-time linearly homomorphic SPS scheme  $\Sigma = (\text{KeyGen}, \text{Sign}, \text{Verify})$  is secure if no adversary has non-negligible advantage in the following game:

- 1. The adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  outputs an integer n, sends it to the challenger  $\mathcal{C}$ . The challenger generates  $(vk, sk) \leftarrow \mathsf{Setup}(1^{\lambda}, n)$  and sends the public verification key back to  $\mathcal{A}$ .
- 2. The adversary A has access to the signing oracle
  - $\operatorname{Sign}(sk,\cdot)$ : A can request the challenger  $\mathcal{C}$  to sign the message vectors  $\{\vec{m}_i\}_{i=1}^{Q_s}$  where  $Q_s$  denotes the number of signing queries.
- 3. A outputs  $(\vec{m}^*, \sigma_*)$ . The adversary wins if and only if  $Verify(vk, \vec{m}^*, \sigma_*) = 1$  and  $\vec{m}^* \notin Span(\{\vec{m}_i\}_{i=1}^{Q_s})$ .

We recall the following construction of the one-time linearly homomorphic structure-preserving signature scheme.

- LHSPS.Setup (Gr, n):
  - 1. Parse Gr as  $(\mathbb{G}, \hat{\mathbb{G}}, \mathbb{G}_T, e)$ .
  - 2. Chose  $\hat{g}_z, \hat{g}_r \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \hat{\mathbb{G}}$ . For  $i \in \{1, \dots, n\}$ , randomly chose  $\chi_i, \gamma_i$  and compute  $\hat{g}_i = \hat{g}_z^{\chi_i} \hat{g}_r^{\gamma_i}$ .
  - 3. Output the verification key  $pk = (\hat{g}_z, \hat{g}_r, \{\hat{g}_i\}^n) \in \hat{\mathbb{G}}^{n+2}$  and the signing key  $sk = (\{\chi_i, \gamma_i\}_{i=1}^n)$ .
- LHSPS.Sign $(vk, sk, \vec{M})$ :
  - 1. Parse the verification key  $vk = (\hat{g}_z, \hat{g}_r, \{\hat{g}_i\}^n) \in \hat{\mathbb{G}}^{n+2}$ , the signing key  $sk = (\{\chi_i, \gamma_i\}_{i=1}^n)$  and the message  $\vec{M} = (M_1, \dots, M_n) \in \mathbb{G}^n$ .

{62}------------------------------------------------

- 2. Output the signature  $\vec{\sigma} = (z, r) \in \mathbb{G}^2$  such that  $z = \prod_{i=1}^n M_i^{\chi_i}$  and  $r = \prod_{i=1}^n M_i^{\gamma_i}$ .
- LHSPS.SignDerive $(vk, (\vec{\sigma}, \{w_i, \vec{\sigma^{(i)}}\}_{i=1}^{\ell}))$ :
  - 1. For all  $i \in \{1, \ldots, \ell\}$ , parse  $\sigma^{(i)}$  as  $(z_i, r_i)$ .
  - 2. Output the signature  $\sigma = (\prod_{i=1}^{\ell} z_i^{w_i}, \prod_{i=1}^{\ell} r_i^{w_i}).$
- LHSPS.Verify( $vk_{\mathsf{LHSPS}}, \sigma$ ):
  - 1. Parse the signature as  $\sigma = (z, r)$  and the message  $\vec{M} = (M_1, \dots, M_n)$ .
  - 2. Return 1 iff  $(M_1, \ldots, M_n) \neq (1_{\mathbb{G}}, \ldots, 1_{\mathbb{G}})$  and the following equation is verified.

$$e(z, \hat{g}_z) \cdot e(r, \hat{g}_r) = \prod_{i=1}^n e(M_i, \hat{g}_i).$$

**Theorem 41 ([LPJY13, Theorem 1]).** The above construction of a one-time linearly homomorphic structure-preserving signature scheme is unforgeable if the SXDH assumption holds in the underlying group.

The above scheme was proven to be unforgeable under the DP assumption, which is implied by the SXDH assumption. As in the remaining part of the construction of RCCA requires SXDH to hold, we state this theorem with SXDH assumption.

**Replayable-CCA encryption scheme.** An RCCA encryption scheme E consists of six PPT algorithms E = (KeyGen, Enc, ReRand, Dec, Verify, AdptPrf). It should verify the following specifications:

- E.KeyGen (Gr): a randomized algorithm which takes as input the group description and outputs an encryption public key pk and a corresponding decryption key dk.
- E.Enc  $(pk, m, \nu)$ : a randomized encryption algorithm which takes as input a public encryption key pk, a plaintext (from a plaintext space), some randomness and outputs a ciphertext.
- E.ReRand  $(pk, c, \nu)$ : a randomized algorithm which takes as input a public key, a ciphertext and some randomness, and outputs another ciphertext.
- E.Dec (dk, c): a deterministic decryption algorithm which takes a decryption key and a ciphertext, and outputs either a plaintext or an error indicator  $\bot$ .
- E.Verify  $(pk, m, \rho, c)$ : a deterministic algorithm which takes as input a public key, a message, some randomness, and a ciphertext and outputs a bit.
- E.AdptPrf  $(ck, pk, c_M, c, (\pi, c_{\nu}), \nu')$  a randomized algorithm which takes as input a commitment key, an encryption public key, a commitment, an equality proof (i.e a Groth-Sahai proof and a commitment), a ciphertext, a proof, some randomness, and outputs an equality proof.

We give the following explicit construction of the RCCA scheme supporting encryption of vectors of group elements.

{63}------------------------------------------------

 $\mathsf{E}.\mathsf{KeyGen}\left( Gr\right) :$ 

- 1. Parse Gr as  $(\mathbb{G}, \hat{\mathbb{G}}, \mathbb{G}_T, e)$ .
- 2. Choose two random group elements  $f, g \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{G}^2$ .
- 3. Choose random exponents  $\{\alpha_i\}_{i=1}^n \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  and compute  $\{h_i\}_{i=1}^n = g^{\alpha_i}$ .
- 4. Generate the Groth-Sahai crs  $c\vec{r}s_{GS}$  by choosing random  $\vec{u}_1, \vec{u}_2 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{G}^2$  and  $\hat{\vec{u}}_1, \hat{\vec{u}}_2 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \hat{\mathbb{G}}^2$ .
- 5. Define two vectors  $\vec{v}_1, \vec{v}_2$  such that

$$\vec{v}_1 = (f, g, 1, 1, \dots, 1) \in \mathbb{G}^{n+2}$$
  $\vec{v}_2 = (1, 1, 1, h_1, \dots, h_n) \in \mathbb{G}^{n+2}$ 

then generate two LHSPS signatures  $\sigma_{\vec{v}_1}$  and  $\sigma_{\vec{v}_2}$  which will be used to proof that a vector is in the  $Span(\vec{v}_1, \vec{v}_2)$ . together with the signing key  $t\vec{k}$ .

6. Output the decryption key  $dk = \alpha$  and the public key

$$pk = (f, g, \{h^{\alpha_i}\}_{i=1}^n, c\vec{r}s_{GS}, \sigma_{\mathsf{LHSPS}} = (\sigma_{\vec{v}_1}, \sigma_{\vec{v}_2})).$$

Notice that the LHSPS signing key  $t\vec{k}$  will never be published by the key generation algorithm, it will only be used in the security proofs.

E.Enc  $(pk, m, \nu)$ :

- 1. Randomly pick a number  $\theta \in \mathbb{Z}_p$ . Compute  $\vec{C} = (c_0, c_1, \dots, c_{n+1}) = (f^{\theta}, g^{\theta}, M_1 \cdot h_1^{\theta}, \dots, M_n \cdot h_n^{\theta})$ .
- 2. Define the bit b=1 and denote  $G=g^b\in\mathbb{G}$  and  $\hat{G}=\hat{g}^b\in\hat{\mathbb{G}}$ .
- 3. Generate the Groth-Sahai proof  $\pi_b$  of

$$e(G, \hat{g}) = e(g, \hat{G})$$

4. For all  $i \in \{1, \dots n+1\}$ , compute  $\Theta_i = c_i^b$ . Compute also the Groth-Sahai  $\pi_{\Theta}$  proof of the equations:

$$e(\Theta_i, \hat{g}) = e(c_i, \hat{G})$$

- 5. Define the vector  $\vec{v} = (c_0^b, c_1^b, g^{1-b}, c_1^{1-b}, \dots, c_{n+1}^{1-b})$ . Generate a LHSPS signature  $\sigma_{\vec{v}}$  such that  $\vec{v} \in Span(\vec{v}_1, \vec{v}_2)$ .
- 6. Compute a Groth-Sahai proof  $\pi_{\vec{v}}$  of the validity of the LHSPS signature  $\sigma_{\vec{v}}$ .
- 7. To enable the re-randomization, compute

$$(F, G, \{H_i\}_{i=1}^n) = (f^b, g^b, \{h_i^b\}_{i=1}^n)$$

and Groth-Sahai proof  $\pi_{FGH}$  of them.

- 8. Define the vector  $\vec{w} = (f^b, g^b, 1, h_1^{1-b}, \dots, h_n^{1-b})$ . Compute a LHSPS signature  $\sigma_{\vec{w}}$  of the fact that  $\vec{w} \in Span(\vec{v}_1, \vec{v}_2)$ .
- 9. Generate a Groth-Sahai proof  $\pi_{\vec{w}}$  of the validity of LHSPS signature  $\sigma_{\vec{w}}$ .
- 10. Output the ciphertext  $c = (\{c_i\}_{i=1}^n, \pi_b, \pi_\theta, \pi_{\vec{v}}, \pi_{FGH}, \pi_{\vec{w}}).$

E.ReRand  $(pk, c, \nu)$ :

{64}------------------------------------------------

- 1. Parse  $c = (\{c_i\}_{i=1}^{n+1}, \pi_b, \pi_\theta, \pi_{\vec{v}}, \pi_{FGH}, \pi_{\vec{w}}).$ 2. Compute  $c'_0 = c_0 \cdot f^{\nu}, c'_1 = c_1 \cdot g^{\nu}$  and for  $i \in \{2, \ldots, n+1\}$ , compute  $c_i' = c_i \cdot h_{i-1}^{\nu}.$
- 3. We update the proof  $\pi_b, \pi_\theta$  using the commitment  $C_F, C_G, C_H$  in  $\pi_{FGH}$ to get  $\pi'_b, \pi'_{\theta}$ .
- 4. We update the commitment of the LHSPS signature  $C'_{\sigma_{\vec{v}}} = C_{\sigma_{\vec{v}}} \cdot C^{\nu}_{\sigma_{\vec{v}}}$ and the update the proof  $\pi_{\vec{v}}$  accordingly to get  $\pi'_{\vec{v}}$ .
- 5. We re-randomize all the updated Groth-Sahai proofs

$$\pi_b', \pi_{\theta}', \pi_{\vec{v}}', \pi_{FGH}, \pi_{\vec{w}}$$

to get the new proofs  $\pi''_b, \pi''_{\vec{v}}, \pi''_{\vec{v}}, \pi''_{FGH}, \pi''_{\vec{w}}$ . 6. Output the new ciphertext  $c' = (\{c'_i\}_{i=1}^n, \pi''_b, \pi''_{\vec{v}}, \pi''_{\vec{v}}, \pi''_{FGH}, \pi''_{\vec{w}})$ .

### E.Dec (dk, c):

- 1. Parse c as  $\sigma = (\{c_i\}_{i=1}^n, \pi_b, \pi_\theta, \pi_{\vec{v}}, \pi_{FGH}, \pi_{\vec{w}}).$
- 2. Check all proofs  $(\pi_b, \pi_{\theta}, \pi_{\vec{v}}, \pi_{FGH}, \pi_{\vec{w}})$  are valid.
- 3. For  $i \in \{1, ..., n\}$ , compute  $M_i = c_{i+1}/(c_1^{\alpha_i})$ .
- 4. Output  $\{M_i\}_{i=1}^n$ .

### E.Verify $(pk, \vec{m}, \nu, c)$ :

- 1. Parse c as  $\sigma = (\{c_i\}_{i=1}^n, \pi_b, \pi_\theta, \pi_{\vec{v}}, \pi_{FGH}, \pi_{\vec{w}}).$
- 2. Verify that  $\pi_b, \pi_\theta, \pi_{\vec{v}}, \pi_{FGH}, \pi_{\vec{w}}$  are all correct.
- 3. Verify the following pairing equations:

$$c_0 = g^{\nu}$$
  $c_1 = f^{\nu}$   $c_{i+1} = h^{\nu} \cdot m_i$ .

where  $i \in \{1, ..., n\}$ .

#### E.AdptPrf $(ck, pk, c_M, c, (\pi, c_{\nu}), \nu')$ :

- 1. We just update the Groth-Sahai proof the new randomness  $\nu'$  by multiplying  $c'_{\nu} = c_{\nu} \cdot \hat{g}^{\nu}$ .
- 2. As the equality proofs consists of the following pairing equations:

$$c_0 = g^{\nu}$$
  $c_1 = f^{\nu}$   $c_{i+1} = h^{\nu} \cdot m_i$ .

where  $i \in \{1, ..., n\}$ .

| Encryption key             | $(10+n)\mathbb{G}+4\hat{\mathbb{G}}$                   |
|----------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------|
| Decryption key             | $n\mathbb{Z}_p$                                        |
| Ciphertext                 | $(6n+19)\mathbb{G} + (16+4n)\hat{\mathbb{G}}$          |
| Verification equations     | $2 \operatorname{linear} + n \operatorname{quadratic}$ |
| Size of the equality proof | $(2+2n)\mathbb{G} + (2+4n)\hat{\mathbb{G}}$            |

*Proof* (of Theorem 16). The completeness and the correctness of the above RCCA encryption scheme are straightforward to verify. We will focusing on the Replayable-CCA property.

We proceed by the series of hybrid games  $\mathsf{Game}_0, \ldots, \mathsf{Game}_5$ , we denote by  $Adv_i$  the advantage of the adversary A to win the game  $Game_i$ .

{65}------------------------------------------------

Game<sub>0</sub>: We have Game<sub>0</sub> is identical to the original RCCA security game and thus by definition:

$$\mathsf{Adv}_0 = \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathtt{RCCA}}_{\mathcal{A}}(1^\lambda)$$

 $\mathsf{Game}_1$ : In this game, we will modify the challenge ciphertext provided to the adversary in the RCCA security game. The new challenge ciphertext is:

$$\boldsymbol{c}^{\star} = (\{c_i^{\star}\}_{i=1}^n, \pi_b^{\star}, \pi_{\theta}^{\star}, \pi_{\vec{v}}^{\star}, \pi_{FGH}^{\star}, \pi_{\vec{w}}^{\star})$$

We only modify  $\pi_{\vec{v}}^{\star}$  and  $\pi_{\vec{w}}^{\star}$ . Instead of generating these two proofs using the signing key  $(\sigma_{\vec{v}_1}, \sigma_{\vec{v}_2})$  of the LHSPS, we will use the signing key td to directly compute the signatures of  $\vec{v}^{\star}$  and  $\vec{w}$ , where  $\vec{v}^{\star} = (1, 1, g, c_2, \dots, c_{n+1})$ . (Notice that the secret signing key is never used in the real game.)

As this change is only conceptional, the distribution of the challenge ciphertext is identical in  $\mathsf{Game}_1$  as in  $\mathsf{Game}_0$ . We have  $\mathsf{Adv}_1 = \mathsf{Adv}_0$ 

Game<sub>2</sub>: In this game, we modify the  $c\vec{r}s$  of the Groth-Sahai proof system. We generate two random values  $\xi, \zeta \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ , then compute  $\vec{u}_1, \vec{u}_2, \hat{\vec{u}}_1, \hat{\vec{u}}_2$  such that  $\vec{u}_1 = \vec{u}_2^{\xi}$  and  $\hat{\vec{u}}_1 = \hat{\vec{u}}_2^{\zeta}$ .

Notice that this is the perfect sound setting of the Groth-Sahai proof system.  $\xi$  and  $\zeta$  can be used to extract the witness. Since the only difference between  $\mathsf{Game}_1$  and  $\mathsf{Game}_2$  is the change of  $\vec{u}_1, \vec{u}_2, \hat{\vec{u}}_1, \hat{\vec{u}}_2$ , the indistinguishability can be proven using the SXDH assumption. Thus, we have  $\mathsf{Adv}_2 \leq \mathsf{Adv}_1 + 2 \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{SXDH}$ .

Game<sub>3</sub>: In this game, we modify the decryption oracle. We will add a manual verification of the underlying LHSPS for the decryption queries. To do this, since the Groth-Sahai proof is settled in the soundness mode  $(\vec{u}_1 = \vec{u}^\xi)$  and  $\hat{u}_1 = \hat{u}_2^\zeta$ . We can use the trapdoors  $\xi, \zeta$  to extract the witness in the commitments of the Groth-Sahai proof. We extract  $\vec{v}$  and  $\sigma_{\vec{v}} = (z, r)$  from the proof  $\pi_{\vec{v}}$ . We use the signing key td of the linearly homomorphic structure-preserving signature  $\sigma_{\vec{v}}^{\dagger} = (z^{\dagger}, r^{\dagger})$  to generate a signature  $\sigma_{\vec{v}}^{\dagger}$  of the vector  $\vec{v}$ . The challenger will reject the decryption query if  $\sigma_{\vec{v}}^{\dagger} \neq \sigma_{\vec{v}}$ .

We can see that, if an adversary can distinguish  $\mathsf{Game}_3$  from  $\mathsf{Game}_2$  then he can forge a valid signature of the underlying LHSPS. Since the unforgeability of the LHSPS is based on the SXDH problem, we have  $\mathsf{Adv}_3 \leq \mathsf{Adv}_2 + \mathsf{Adv}_{DP}(1^{\lambda})$ .

Game<sub>4</sub>: We will modify all the decryption oracles (both pre-challenge and post-challenge ones) to avoid the use of  $\log_g(h_i) = \alpha_i$ . After making these changes, we can modify the generation of  $h_i$  to  $h_i = f^{x_i}g^{y_i}$ .

Pre-challenge decryption queries: We use the trapdoor of the Groth-Sahai proof to extract the witness of the proof, if we have b=0 then we directly reject the proof.

Post-challenge decryption queries: We also use the trapdoor of the Groth-Sahai proof to extract the witness of the proof, if b=0 and the ciphertext is not rejected by the rule of  $\mathsf{Game}_3$ , the challenger outputs  $\mathsf{Replay}$ . Additionally, both in pre-challenge and post-challenge decryption queries.

{66}------------------------------------------------

Since we don't have  $\alpha_i$  anymore, we decrypt the ciphertext by computing  $M_i = c_{i+1}/(c_0^{x_i} \cdot c_1^{y^i})$ .

We now analyse the change of the decryption oracles:

Pre-challenge: It is easy to see that in case of b=0, the challenger only issued two LHSPS signatures of  $\vec{v}_1$  and  $\vec{v}_2$ . And the vector  $\vec{v}$  is clearly not in the span of  $Span(\vec{v}_1, \vec{v}_2)$ . So the adversary is statistically impossible to forge a correct signature.

Post-challenge: Note that the Groth-Sahai proof is in the perfect soundness setting of the Groth-Sahai proof, thus the challenger  $\mathcal{C}$  can use the trapdoor to extract all the witness used in the proof. We will now separate two case:

- If  $g^b = 1$ , we have  $\vec{v} = (c_0, c_1, 1, 1, ..., 1)$ . But  $\vec{c}$  is not rejected in the Game<sub>3</sub>, with a overwhelming probability, we will have  $\vec{v} \in Span(\vec{v}_1)$ . Thus we have  $M_i = c_{i+1}/(c_0^x \cdot c_1^y)$ .
- If  $g^b = 0$ , we have  $\vec{v} = (1, 1, g, c_2, \dots, c_{n+1})$ . As the third element is  $g, \vec{v} = \vec{v} \cdot \vec{v}_2^{\theta} \cdot \vec{w}^{\rho}$ . This means that  $\vec{v}$  is a randomization of  $\vec{v}^*$ , thus we can answer Replay to the adversary.

Game<sub>5</sub>: We modify the distribution of the challenge ciphertext. Instead of choosing them as an encryption of  $\vec{M}_0$  or  $\vec{M}_1$ . We Choose them all random elements. By the self-rerandomizability of the DDH assumption in  $\mathbb{G}$ , the game 5 is indistinguishable from the game 4.

During the  $\mathsf{Game}_5$ , as the challenge ciphertext is only random group elements, the adversary cannot have more advantage than a random guess.

#### <span id="page-66-0"></span>B.3 Instantiation of the encryption scheme E

```
\begin{split} \text{Let } Gr &= (p, \mathbb{G}, g). \\ \text{E.KeyGen}(): \\ &- (dk_1, dk_2) \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^2 \\ &- \text{Return } ((g^{dk_1}, g^{dk_2}), (dk_1, dk_2)) \\ \text{E.Enc}((D_1, D_2), (M_1, M_2), \nu): \\ &- \text{Return } (g^{\nu}, M_1 \cdot D_1^{\nu}, M_2 \cdot D_2^{\nu}) \\ \text{E.ReRand}((D_1, D_2), (C_0, C_1, C_2), \nu): \\ &- \text{Return } (C_0 \cdot g^{\nu}, C_1 \cdot D_1^{\nu}, C_2 \cdot D_2^{\nu}) \\ \text{E.Dec}((dk_1, dk_2), (C_0, C_1, C_2)): \\ &- \text{Return } (C_0 \cdot C_1^{dk_1}, C_2 \cdot C_0^{dk_2}) \\ \text{E.Verify}((D_1, D_2), (M_1, M_2), \nu, (C_0, C_1, C_2)): \\ &- \text{Return } (g^{\nu}, M_1 \cdot D_1^{\nu}, M_2 \cdot D_2^{\nu}) = (C_0, C_1, C_2) \\ \text{E.AdptPrf}(ck, ek, (com_{M_1}, com_{M_2}), c, \tilde{\pi} = (\pi, com_{\nu}), \nu'): \\ &- \text{Analog to } \mathbf{B}.2 \end{split}
```

**Proposition 42.** If there exists an adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  that breaks the IACR property of the scheme with advantage  $\epsilon_{\text{IACR}}$ , then there exists an adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  that breaks SXDH with advantage  $\epsilon_{\text{SXDH}}$ , with

$$\epsilon_{\text{IACR}} \leq 4 \epsilon_{\text{SXDH}}$$
.

{67}------------------------------------------------

We define the following experiments:

```
\mathbf{Expt}^{\mathtt{IACR}}_{\mathcal{A},b}((\mathbb{G},g,p)):
     ((P_1,P_2),(dk_1,dk_2)) \leftarrow \mathsf{KeyGen}(Gr)
     ((C_0^{(0)}, C_1^{(0)}, C_2^{(0)}), (C_0^{(1)}, C_1^{(1)}, C_2^{(1)})) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}((P_1, P_2))
     \nu \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_n
     (C_0, C_1, C_2) \leftarrow (C_0^{(b)} \cdot g^{\nu}, C_1^{(b)} \cdot P_1^{\nu}, C_2^{(b)} \cdot P_2^{\nu})
     b' \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(C_0, C_1, C_2)
     Return b'
\mathbf{Expt}^{\mathtt{IACR}V2}_{\mathcal{A},b}((\mathbb{G},g,p)):
      ((P_1,P_2),(dk_1,dk_2)) \leftarrow \mathsf{KeyGen}(Gr)
     ((C_0^{(0)}, C_1^{(0)}, C_2^{(0)}), (C_0^{(1)}, C_1^{(1)}, C_2^{(1)})) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}((P_1, P_2))
     \nu, \nu_2 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p
     (C_0, C_1, C_2) \leftarrow (C_0^{(b)} \cdot g^{\nu}, C_1^{(b)} \cdot P_1^{\nu_2}, C_2^{(b)} \cdot P_2^{\nu})
b' \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(C_0, C_1, C_2)
      Return b'
\mathbf{Expt}^{\mathtt{IACR}V3}_{\mathcal{A},b}((\mathbb{G},g,p)):
     ((P_1, P_2), (dk_1, dk_2)) \leftarrow \mathsf{KeyGen}(Gr)
     ((C_0^{(0)}, C_1^{(0)}, C_2^{(0)}), (C_0^{(1)}, C_1^{(1)}, C_2^{(1)})) \leftarrow \mathcal{A}((P_1, P_2))
     \nu, \nu_2, \nu_3 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p
     (C_0, C_1, C_2) \leftarrow (C_0^{(b)} \cdot g^{\nu}, C_1^{(b)} \cdot P_1^{\nu_2}, C_2^{(b)} \cdot P_2^{\nu_3})
     b' \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(C_0, C_1, C_2)
      Return b'
```

By noticing that  $|\Pr(\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},b}^{\mathtt{IACR}}((\mathbb{G},g,p))=1) - \Pr(\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},b}^{\mathtt{IACR}V2}((\mathbb{G},g,p))=1)|$ and  $|\Pr(\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},b}^{\mathtt{IACR}V2}((\mathbb{G},g,p))=1) - \Pr(\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},b}^{\mathtt{IACR}V3}((\mathbb{G},g,p))=1|$  are less or equal to  $\epsilon_{\mathrm{SXDH}}$ , and because  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},0}^{\mathtt{IACR}V3}((\mathbb{G},g,p))$  and  $\mathbf{Expt}_{\mathcal{A},1}^{\mathtt{IACR}V3}((\mathbb{G},g,p))$  are distributed equally, we deduce  $\epsilon_{\mathrm{IACR}} \leq 4 \epsilon_{\mathrm{SXDH}}$ .

### <span id="page-67-1"></span>C Efficiency analysis

We summarize the efficiency of the the building blocks C, S, S' and E in Tables 1, 2 and 3, where "m-s" stands for "multi-scalar".

### <span id="page-67-0"></span>D Computational assumptions

**Definition 43 (SXDH).** The Symmetric External Diffie-Hellman Assumption states that given  $(g^r, g^s, g^t)$  for random  $r, s \in \mathbb{Z}_p$ , it is hard to decide whether t = rs or t is random; moreover, given  $(\hat{g}^{r'}, \hat{g}^{s'}, \hat{g}^{t'})$  for random  $r', s' \in \mathbb{Z}_p$ , it is hard to decide whether t' = r's' or t' is random.

The Asymetric Double Hidden Strong Diffie Hellman (ADHSDH) assumption and the Asymetric Weak Flexible Computational Diffie Hellman (AWFCDH) assumption have been introduced in  $[AFG^+10]$ .

{68}------------------------------------------------

<span id="page-68-0"></span>Table 1. Sizes of components of the commit-and-prove scheme C

**Definition 44 (q-ADHSDH).** Given  $(g, f, k, x = g^{\xi}, \hat{g}) \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{G}^4 \times \hat{\mathbb{G}}$  and  $\hat{y} = \hat{g}^{\xi}$  and  $(a_i = (kg^{\omega_i})^{\frac{1}{\xi+\gamma_i}}, c_i = f^{\gamma_i}, v_i = g^{\omega_i}, \hat{d}_i = \hat{g}^{\gamma_i}, \hat{w}_i = \hat{g}^{\omega_i})_{i=1}^q$ , for  $\gamma_i, \omega_i \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ , it is hard to output a new tuple  $(a, c, v, \hat{d}, \hat{w}) \in \mathbb{G}^3 \times \hat{\mathbb{G}}^2$  of this form, i.e., a tuple that satisfies

$$e(a,\hat{y}\hat{d}) = e(kv,\hat{g}) \ \wedge \ e(c,\hat{g}) = e(f,\hat{d}) \ \wedge \ e(v,\hat{g}) = e(g,\hat{w}).$$

**Definition 45 (AWFCDH).** Given random generators  $(g, a = g^{\alpha}, \hat{g}) \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} (\mathbb{G}^{*})^{2} \times \hat{\mathbb{G}}$ , it is hard to output  $(g^{\nu}, g^{\nu\alpha}, \hat{g}^{\nu}, \hat{g}^{\nu\alpha})$ , i.e., a tuple  $(r, m, \hat{s}, \hat{n})$  that satisfies:

$$e(a, \hat{s}) = e(m, \hat{g}) \wedge e(m, \hat{g}) = e(g, \hat{n}) \wedge e(r, \hat{g}) = e(g, \hat{s}).$$
